Wiping over Cotton Socks – The Dispute and Its Resolution
Conditions for wiping over jorbeen and dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions required for wiping over cotton socks according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position and explain how the intra-madhhab dispute was resolved.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa initially required leather lining or soles for wiping over cotton socks, but later retracted to the Sahibayn's view: thick, waterproof, and walkable socks suffice.

Wiping over socks (mash 'ala al-khuffayn) is a well-known concession in wudu. But what about cotton socks? The Hanafi school has a nuanced history: Imam Abu Hanifa initially imposed strict requirements, while his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), advocated a more lenient position. Through evidence and scholarly reflection, the school eventually reached a consensus. This lesson unpacks the conditions, the proofs, and how the dispute was settled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being discussed: wiping over cotton socks during wudu. State the general ruling (permissible) and note that it is a substitute for washing the feet.
2
State Abu Hanifa's initial position
Abu Hanifa required that cotton socks be mujalladayn (entirely covered with hide) or mu'allayn (soled with leather).
This was based on specific hadiths mentioning socks with leather components.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn allowed wiping over any thick cotton socks meeting three conditions: thickness preventing water seepage, ability to stay on without tying, and walkability for about a mile.
Their reasoning included general hadiths and qiyas with leather socks.
4
Examine the evidence for each view
Analyze the hadith of Mughirah and the report of Anas (used by Abu Hanifa) versus the general hadiths and qiyas (used by the Sahibayn).
5
Understand the tarjih and resolution
Imam Abu Hanifa retracted to the view of the Sahibayn in his later life, leading to consensus. The mufta bihi position is therefore the Sahibayn's three conditions.

Source Text

ويجوز المسح على الجوربين الا ان يكونا مجلدين او منعلين وقالا لا يجوز اذا كا نا ثخينين لا يشفان
تشریح سوت کے موزے کو جور بین یا جراب کہتے ہیں۔ اس کے تلے پر چمڑا چڑھا ہوا ہو تو اس کو منعلین کہتے ہیں۔ یہ فعل سے مشتق ہے۔ جوتے کی ایڑی میں جو لو ہالگاتے ہیں اس کو فعل کہتے ہیں۔ اور تلے میں بھی چھڑا ہو اور جوتے کی طرح قدم پر بھی چمڑا ہوتو چونکہ کافی چمڑا لگ گیا اس لئے سوت کے اس موزے کو مجلد ین کہتے ہیں۔ جواب مجلدین ہوں یا متعلمین ہو تب ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ان پر مسح کرنا جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں۔
للبيهة
عن مغيرة بن شعبة قال توضا النبي الا الله ومسح على الجوربين والنعلين (الف ) ( ترمذی شریف، باب فی المسح على الجور بین والمعلمین ج اول ص ۲۹ نمبر ۹۹ ابوداؤد، باب المسح علی الجور بین ص ۲۴ نمبر ۱۵۹) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جور بین پر مسح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور والنعلين کا ترجمہ استاذ ابو الولید نے یہ کیا ہے جور بین جو منعلین ہو یعنی ایسا سوت کا موزہ جس میں نل لگا ہواہو۔ اور راشد بن حج سے روایت ہے قال رایت انس بن مالك دخل الخلاء وعليه جوربان اسفلهما جلود و اعلاهما خز فمسح عليهما (ب) السنن بیھقی ، باب ماورد فی الجوربین و المعلمین ، ج اول ص ۴۲۸، نمبر ۷ ۱۳۵) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے جو سوت کے موزے میں مجلد ین اور منعلین ہونے کی قید لگائی ہے وہ ان روایات کی روشنی میں لگائی ہے۔ فائدہ صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تین شرطیں ہوں تو سوت کے موزے پر مسح جائز ہے (۱) اتنا موٹا ہو کہ مسح کرتے وقت پانی پاؤں کی خال تک سرایت نہ کرتا ہو (۲) بغیر باندھے پاؤں پر رکھتا ہو (۳) ایک میل تک موزے میں چل سکتا ہو۔ تو اس موزے پر مسح کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ان شرطوں سے سوت کا موزہ چمڑے کے موزے کے مشابہ ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اصل میں چمڑے کے موزے پر مسح کرنا جائز ہے اس لئے یہ شرطیں لگائی گئیں۔ (۲) عام احادیث سے جور بین پر مسح کرنے کا ثبوت ہے چاہے مجلد ین اور معلمین ہو یا نہ ہو ۔ اس لئے خالص جور بین پر مذکورہ شرطوں کے ساتھ مسح کرنا جائز ہے۔
امام ابو حنیفہ نے آخری عمر میں صاحبین کے قول کی طرف رجوع کیا ہے۔ اس لئے جور بین پر مسح کرنے کا اتفاق ہو گیا۔ خف : چھڑے کا موزہ، جوربین : سوت کا موزہ جس کے تلے میں چھڑا لگا ہوا ہوں، مخینین : مخین کا تثنیہ ہے موٹا موزہ، یشفان : تثنیہ ہے یشف کا جس میں پانی چھن جاتا ہو۔
It is permissible to wipe over jorbeen (cotton socks) unless they are mujalladayn (covered with hide) or mu'allayn (soled). And they (the Sahibayn) said: it is not permissible unless they are thick (thikheen) and water does not seep through (la yashifaan). Explanation: A cotton sock is called jorbayn or jirab. If leather is attached to its sole, it is called mu'allayn (soled). The word 'nall' is derived from 'na'l' meaning shoe sole. If both the sole and the upper part of the foot are covered with leather, it is called mujalladayn (hide-covered). So if they are mujalladayn or mu'allayn, then according to Abu Hanifa wiping over them is permissible; otherwise not. Of the hadith: from Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) performed wudu and wiped over the jorbeen and the nallayn (slippers/soled socks).' (Tirmidhi, Bab al-Mash 'ala al-Jorbeen wa al-Mu'allamin, vol 1 p 29 no 99; Abu Dawood, Bab al-Mash 'ala al-Jorbeen, p 24 no 159) This shows that wiping over jorbeen is permissible. The translation of 'nallayn' by Ustad Abu al-Walid is 'jorbeen that are mu'allayn', i.e., cotton socks with soles. And from Rashid ibn Hujr: 'I saw Anas ibn Malik enter the toilet wearing two jorbeen, the lower part of which were leather and the upper part khazz (silk/wool), and he wiped over them.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab ma warada fi al-Jorbeen wa al-Mu'allamin, vol 1 p 428 no 1357) This shows that Imam Abu Hanifa's condition of mujalladayn or mu'allayn is based on these reports. Benefit: The Sahibayn and the three Imams (other schools) say that three conditions are necessary for wiping over cotton socks: (1) they are thick so that when wiping, water does not seep through to the skin; (2) they stay on the feet without tying; (3) one can walk a mile in them. So with these conditions, wiping is permissible. The reasoning is that these conditions make the cotton socks similar to leather socks, and since wiping over leather socks is the original ruling, these conditions align them. However, general hadiths prove wiping over jorbeen regardless of mujalladayn or mu'allayn, so pure jorbeen with these conditions are permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted to the view of the Sahibayn, so there is consensus on this. Glossary: khuff = leather sock; jorbeen = cotton sock with leather sole; mukhayanin = thick socks (dual); yashifan = dual of yashif meaning that water seeps through.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over the conditions for wiping over cotton socks (jorbeen). The matn states that wiping over jorbeen is permissible unless they are mujalladayn (entirely covered with hide) or mu'allayn (soled). This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) held that wiping is permissible even without these conditions, provided the socks are thick and water does not seep through. The Urdu commentary explains the terminology: a cotton sock with a leather sole is 'mu'allayn'; one with both sole and upper covered in leather is 'mujalladayn'. Abu Hanifa's condition is based on specific hadiths like those of Mughirah and Anas, which describe socks with leather parts. The Sahibayn and the three other Imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) allow wiping over any thick cotton socks that meet three conditions: sufficient thickness, ability to stay on without tying, and ability to walk in them. The commentary notes that Imam Abu Hanifa in his later life retracted to the view of the Sahibayn, resulting in consensus (ittifaq) that wiping over such thick cotton socks is permissible. Thus, the operative ruling today is the one held by the Sahibayn, with the three conditions.

Key Terms
جوربین (jorbeen): Cotton socks that cover the foot; in this text, specifically those that may have leather components.
مجلدین (mujalladayn): Socks that are entirely covered with hide or leather.
منعلین (mu'allayn): Socks that have a leather sole (like a shoe bottom).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on wiping over pure cotton socks without leather?
A) Not permissible under any condition.
B) Permissible if they are thick, waterproof, and walkable.
C) Permissible only if they are mujalladayn.
D) Permissible only if mu'allayn.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits wiping over cotton socks that meet the three conditions of thickness, waterproofness, and walkability, based on the consensus after Abu Hanifa's retraction.

Impermissibility of Wiping Over Headgear and Gloves in Wudu
Ruling that wiping over headgear and gloves is not allowed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over turban, cap, veil, and gloves, and explain the dalil and usul principle that justify it.

Core Idea
Wiping over headgear or gloves invalidates wudu because the Qur'an commands direct wiping of the head and washing of the hands.

You have learned that wiping over leather socks (khuff) is permissible. But does that extend to headgear or gloves? This lesson examines a critical Hanafi ruling: wiping over a turban, cap, face veil, or gloves is not valid. The proof is not based on a single hadith but on the Qur'anic text itself and a foundational usul principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over a turban (imamah), cap (qalansuwah), face veil (burqa), or gloves (dastanay) during wudu instead of wiping the head or washing the face/hands. The ruling: not permissible (haram/ invalid).
The ruling applies equally to men and women.
2
Locate the primary dalil: the Qur'an
The Qur'anic verse of wudu (al-Ma'idah 5:6) commands: '...and wipe your heads...' (wa imsahu bi ru'usikum). This is a clear imperative ordering direct wiping of the head.
The verse uses the preposition 'bi' which indicates a partial wiping of the head, but it must be directly on the skin or hair.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle regarding ahad hadith
The Hanafi school holds that a hadith that is ahad (single-transmitter) cannot abrogate or add to the clear text of the Qur'an. Therefore, any hadith that seems to permit wiping over a turban must be interpreted in a way that does not contradict the verse, e.g., the Prophet ﷺ would wipe his head and include a minimal part of the turban, or the turban was partially unwrapped.
This principle distinguishes Hanafis from Shafi'is, who allow wiping over a turban based on ahad hadith.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school permits wiping over a turban (if part of the head is exposed) based on hadith reports. The Hanafi response: those reports are interpreted as exceptional or do not establish a general rule. The verse remains primary.
The ruling for face veil and gloves is even stronger because the face and hands are to be washed, not wiped.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi position
The established (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that wiping over these items is not valid. If someone does so intentionally, the wudu is invalid and must be repeated.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Source Text

ولا يجوز المسح [على العمامة ولا على القلنسوة ولا على البرقع ولا على الجوربين] (١٢) عمامہ پر ٹوپی پر اور برقع پر اور دستانے پر مسح جائز نہیں ہے۔ (۱) آیت میں سر پر مسح کرنے کا حکم دیا ہے اب خبر آحاد حدیث کے ذریعہ سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے احادیث کی وجہ سے پگڑی، ٹوپی اور برقع پر مسح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور جن احادیث میں اس کا ذکر ہے کہ آپ نے پگڑی پر مسح کیا اس کا مطلب یہ ہے
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے وضو فر مایا اور سوت کے موزے پر اور چپل پر مسح فرمایا، یا چپل کے ساتھ مسح فرمایا (ب) میں نے انس بن مالک کو دیکھا کہ بیت الخلاء میں داخل ہوئے اور آپ کے پاؤں میں دوسوت کے موزے تھے ۔ دونوں کے نیچے کا حصہ چھڑے کا تھا اور اوپر کا حصہ ریشم تھا تو آپ نے دونوں پر سح فرمایا۔
And it is not permissible to wipe over the turban, nor over the cap, nor over the veil, nor over the gloves. (12) It is not permissible to wipe over the turban, cap, burqa, and gloves. (1) The verse commands wiping the head; it is not allowed to add to the Book of Allah through ahad hadith. Therefore, wiping over the turban, cap, and burqa is not permissible. And the hadiths that mention the Prophet wiping over his turban are interpreted (otherwise). Footnotes: (a) He performed wudu and wiped over the cotton socks and slippers, or wiped with slippers. (b) I saw Anas ibn Malik enter the toilet wearing two cotton socks, the lower part of which were leather and the upper part silk, and he wiped over them.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling that wiping over headgear (turban, cap), face veil (burqa), and gloves is not permissible in wudu. The proof is rooted in the Qur'anic verse of wudu (al-Ma'idah: 6), which explicitly commands wiping the head (bi ru'usikum). The Hanafi principle stated here is that it is not permissible to add to the commands of the Qur'an through a hadith that is ahad (single-transmitter). The ahad hadith that report the Prophet wiping over his turban are interpreted in a way that does not contradict the verse, such as considering that the turban was partially unwrapped and the forehead was wiped, or that the wiping was over the head and the turban was just included minimally. This ruling is distinct from the permissibility of wiping over khuff (leather socks), which is based on multiple ahadith and qiyas, but headgear takes a different ruling because the original command is to wipe the head directly. The footnote hadiths are somewhat misplaced but relate to wiping over socks. The lesson emphasizes that the Hanafi school strictly follows the Qur'anic text and does not allow substitution for head wiping via ahad reports alone.

Key Terms
عمامة (imamah): Turban worn on the head; wiping over it instead of the head is not permissible.
قلنسوة (qalansuwah): A cap or head covering; wiping over it is not permissible.
برقع (burqa): Face veil; wiping over it is not permissible as it covers the face (which is washed, not wiped).
دستانے (dastanay (Persian/Urdu)): Gloves; wiping over them is not permissible; the hands must be washed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis not permit wiping over a turban in wudu?
A) Because the turban is not made of leather.
B) Because the Qur'an commands wiping the head directly, and ahad hadith cannot override the Qur'an.
C) Because turbans were not worn during the time of the Prophet.
D) Because the Prophet never wiped over a turban.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over headgear or gloves in wudu is invalid because the Qur'an requires direct wiping of the head and washing of the face and hands, and ahad hadith cannot change this.

Wiping Over Woolen Socks: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Consensus
Analyses conditions for wiping over woolen socks with intra-madhhab dispute and resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for wiping over woolen socks according to the Hanafi mufta bihi position and explain how Imam Abu Hanifa's initial view was reconciled with the Sahibayn's view.

Core Idea
Wiping over woolen socks is permissible when they are thick, stay on without tying, and allow walking a mile.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on wiping over woolen socks (jorbain). The passage defines different types of socks and presents a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main students, the Sahibayn. You will learn the conditions that make wiping permissible and understand how the school settled on a final position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi mufta bihi position
Identify the final ruling: wiping over woolen socks is permissible if they meet three conditions: thickness (water does not seep), stay on without tying, and ability to walk one mile.
This is the position of the Sahibayn, adopted by Abu Hanifa later.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Abu Hanifa initially required the socks to be either mun'alayn (leather sole) or mujalladayn (fully leather-covered). This is the view that was later abandoned.
The opponent here is Imam Abu Hanifa's own initial view, not another school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith evidence that Abu Hanifa used: the Prophet wiping over jorbain that were mun'alayn (Tirmidhi) and the practice of Anas ibn Malik with leather-soled socks.
These narrations specifically mention leather parts.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response (Sahibayn's view)
Understand the Sahibayn's reasoning: general hadiths about wiping over jorbain without leather condition, and analogy to leather khuffs through three conditions that make woolen socks similar.
The Sahibayn and the other three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) held this view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa's initial view, only socks with leather parts could be wiped; under the final view, any thick woolen sock meeting the three conditions suffices. Tarjih: Abu Hanifa reverted, making the Sahibayn's view the relied-upon position.
This consensus simplifies the ruling for the community.

ولا يجوز المسح جائز جب کہ موٹے ہوں اور پانی نہ چھنتا ہو۔ تشریح سوت کے موزے کو جور بین یا جراب کہتے ہیں۔ اس کے تلے پر چمڑا چڑھا ہوا ہو تو اس کو منعلین کہتے ہیں۔ یہ فعل سے مشتق ہے۔ جوتے کی ایڑی میں جو لو ہالگاتے ہیں اس کو فعل کہتے ہیں۔ اور تلے میں بھی چھڑا ہو اور جوتے کی طرح قدم پر بھی چمڑا ہوتو چونکہ کافی چمڑا لگ گیا اس لئے سوت کے اس موزے کو مجلد ین کہتے ہیں۔ جواب مجلدین ہوں یا متعلمین ہو تب ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ان پر مسح کرنا جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ للبيهة عن مغيرة بن شعبة قال توضا النبي الا الله ومسح على الجوربين والنعلين (الف ) ( ترمذی شریف، باب فی المسح على الجور بین والمعلمین ج اول ص ۲۹ نمبر ۹۹ ابوداؤد، باب المسح علی الجور بین ص ۲۴ نمبر ۱۵۹) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جور بین پر مسح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور والنعلین کا ترجمہ استاذ ابو الولید نے یہ کیا ہے جور بین جو منعلین ہو یعنی ایسا سوت کا موزہ جس میں نل لگا ہواہو۔ اور راشد بن حج سے روایت ہے قال رایت انس بن مالك دخل الخلاء وعليه جوربان اسفلهما جلود و اعلاهما خز فمسح عليهما (ب) السنن بیھقی ، باب ماورد فی الجوربین و المعلمین ، ج اول ص ۴۲۸، نمبر ۷ ۱۳۵) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے جو سوت کے موزے میں مجلد ین اور منعلین ہونے کی قید لگائی ہے وہ ان روایات کی روشنی میں لگائی ہے۔ فائدہ صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تین شرطیں ہوں تو سوت کے موزے پر مسح جائز ہے (۱) اتنا موٹا ہو کہ مسح کرتے وقت پانی پاؤں کی خال تک سرایت نہ کرتا ہو (۲) بغیر باندھے پاؤں پر رکھتا ہو (۳) ایک میل تک موزے میں چل سکتا ہو۔ تو اس موزے پر مسح کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ان شرطوں سے سوت کا موزہ چمڑے کے موزے کے مشابہ ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اصل میں چمڑے کے موزے پر مسح کرنا جائز ہے اس لئے یہ شرطیں لگائی گئیں۔ (۲) عام احادیث سے جور بین پر مسح کرنے کا ثبوت ہے چاہے مجلد ین اور معلمین ہو یا نہ ہو ۔ اس لئے خالص جور بین پر مذکورہ شرطوں کے ساتھ مسح کرنا جائز ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ نے آخری عمر میں صاحبین کے قول کی طرف رجوع کیا ہے۔ اس لئے جور بین پر مسح کرنے کا اتفاق ہو گیا۔ خف : چھڑے کا موزہ، جوربین : سوت کا موزہ جس کے تلے میں چھڑا لگا ہوا ہوں، مخینین : مخین کا تثنیہ ہے موٹا موزہ، یشفان : تثنیہ ہے یشف کا جس میں پانی چھن جاتا ہو۔
Ruling: Wiping is permissible when they are thick and water does not seep through. Explanation: A woolen sock is called jorbain or jiraab. If its sole is covered with leather, it is called mun'alayn. This is derived from na'l (shoe heel piece). If both sole and upper part are leather, it is mujalladayn (with leather). According to Abu Hanifa, wiping is allowed on mujalladayn or mun'alayn, otherwise not. Evidence: Al-Bayhaqi from Mughirah ibn Shu'bah that the Prophet performed wudoo and wiped over jorbain and na'layn. Tirmidhi, etc. This hadith shows wiping over jorbain is allowed. Abu al-Waleed translated 'wa al-na'layn' as jorbain that are mun'alayn. Also, Rasheed ibn Huj narrates he saw Anas ibn Malik enter the toilet wearing two jorbain, the bottom of which was leather and the top was silk, and he wiped over them. Thus, Abu Hanifa's condition of mujalladayn or mun'alayn is based on these narrations. Benefit: The Sahibayn and the three Imams say that if three conditions are met, wiping is allowed: (1) thick enough that water does not seep to the foot during wiping, (2) stays on foot without tying, (3) one can walk a mile in them. So wiping is allowed. Reason: these conditions make the woolen sock resemble leather socks. Wiping over leather socks is originally allowed. In general hadiths, wiping over jorbain is proven whether they are mujalladayn or not. Therefore, wiping over plain jorbain with the mentioned conditions is allowed. Imam Abu Hanifa in his later years reverted to the view of the Sahibayn, so consensus was reached. Vocabulary: khuff: leather sock, jorbain: woolen sock with leather sole, mukhkhain: dual of mukhkh (thick sock), yashifan: dual of yashif (water seeps through).
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of wiping over woolen socks (jorbain) during wudoo. The author first defines terms: jorbain are woolen socks; mun'alayn are those with leather on the sole; mujalladayn are those with leather on both sole and upper foot. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, wiping is only allowed if the socks are either mun'alayn or mujalladayn. The evidence is from hadiths reported by al-Bayhaqi and others, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped over jorbain that were mun'alayn, and Anas ibn Malik wiped over jorbain that had leather soles. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and the other three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) hold a different view: wiping is permissible on any thick woolen sock that meets three conditions: (1) thick enough that water does not reach the foot, (2) stays on the foot without tying, (3) one can walk a mile in them. The rationale is that these conditions make the sock similar to leather khuffs, which are universally allowed for wiping. The author then notes that Imam Abu Hanifa eventually adopted the view of the Sahibayn, achieving consensus. The passage concludes with vocabulary notes. The teacher should emphasize that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the one of the Sahibayn due to the later consensus.

Key Terms
جوربين (jorbain): A pair of woolen socks, often translated as stockings or socks.
منعلين (mun'alayn): Pair of socks/shoes that have a leather sole attached (like sandals).
مجلدين (mujalladayn): Pair of socks that are fully covered with leather, both sole and upper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi position), what condition is NOT required for wiping over woolen socks?
A) They must be thick so water does not seep through.
B) They must have leather soles (mun'alayn).
C) They must stay on the foot without tying.
D) One must be able to walk a mile in them.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits wiping over thick woolen socks that are self-supporting and walkable, following the Sahibayn's view adopted by Abu Hanifa.

The Ruling on Wiping Over Head and Hand Coverings
States ruling that wiping over head and hand coverings is not permitted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over head and hand coverings during wudoo and explain the proof from the Quran and sunnah.

Core Idea
Wiping over a turban or gloves is not a substitute for wiping the head or washing the hands.

Many Muslims assume that because the Prophet (ﷺ) wiped over his turban, it is sufficient to wipe over any head covering during wudoo. This lesson clarifies that the Prophet also wiped part of his head directly. The Hanafi school maintains that the Quranic command to wipe the head is definitive, and ahad hadith must be interpreted in harmony with it, not as an override. Wiping over a barrier that is easily removed does not fulfill the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that wiping over the turban, cap, burqa, and gloves is not permissible (ja'iz nahi hai). In Hanafi terminology, this means it invalidates the wudoo if done exclusively without direct contact.
The ruling is for acts of wudoo; if one only wipes the covering, the relevant limb is not purified.
2
Locate the primary dalil: the Quranic command
The verse 'wa islahu bi ru'usikum' (Quran 5:6) commands wiping the head. This is a general and unambiguous command, establishing the obligation of direct head contact.
The Hanafi usul principle: a clear Quranic command cannot be overridden by ahad hadith.
3
Interpret the relevant ahadith
Ahadith reporting that the Prophet wiped over his turban are understood to mean he wiped part of his head and then passed his hand over the turban, as shown in Abu Dawood and Muslim narrations. Thus, wiping the turban alone is insufficient.
The key detail: the Prophet inserted his hand under the turban to wipe his head.
4
Recognize scholarly consensus (Ijma)
Imam Tirmidhi reports that the early scholars (Sufyan al-Thawri, Malik, Ibn al-Mubarak, al-Shafi'i) all agree that wiping just the turban is not sufficient without also wiping the head. This consensus strengthens the Hanafi position.
Ijma is a strong proof; here it supports the interpretation.
5
Apply the same reasoning to gloves and other coverings
The same principle extends to hand coverings like gloves: there is no hardship in removing them, so washing the hands is obligatory. Wiping over gloves is not a valid substitute.
This contrasts with the rukhsa (concession) for bandages (jabirah) where hardship is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عمامہ پر ٹوپی پر اور برقع پر اور دستانے پر مسح جائز نہیں ہے۔ (۱) آیت میں سر پر مسح کرنے کا حکم دیا ہے اب خبر آحاد حدیث کے ذریعہ سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے احادیث کی وجہ سے پگڑی، ٹوپی اور برقع پر مسح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور جن احادیث میں اس کا ذکر ہے کہ آپ نے پگڑی پر مسح کیا اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ سر کے بعض حصہ پر مسح کیا اور پگڑی پر بھی کر لیا (۲) چنانچہ حدیث میں اس طریقہ کار کا ثبوت ہے عن انس بن مالك قال رأيت رسول الله له يتوضأ وعليه عمامة قطرية فادخل يده من تحت العمامة فمسح مقدم رأسه فلم ينقض العمامة (الف) ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب اسح علی العمامت ۶۱ نمبر ۱۴۷) مسلم میں ہے ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مسح على الخفين ومقدم رأسه وعلى عمامته ( مسلم شریف، باب امسح علیا لناصية والعمامة، ص ۱۳۴ نمبر ۲۷۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بعض سر پر مسح کیا اور پگڑی پر مسح کیا۔ اس لئے صرف پگڑی پر مسح کافی نہیں ہے (۳) امام ترمندی نے فرمایا کہ علماء فرماتے ہیں کہ صرف عمامہ پر مسح کرنا کافی نہیں ہو گا جب تک اس کے ساتھ سر پر بھی صبح نہ کر لے۔ وحوقول سفیان الثوری و مالک بن انس و ابن المبارک، والشافعی ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی امسح علی الجوربین والعمامۃ ص ۲۹نمبر۱۰۰) (۴) دار قطنی نے با ضابطہ باب باندھا ہے باب فی جواز امسح على بعض الرأس ( ج اول ص ۲۰ نمبر (۷۲) اور اس کے تحت ایسی چار حدیثیں ذکر کی ہیں جس سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ عمامہ کے ساتھ سر پر مسح کرنا ضروری ہے۔ دستانے پر بھی مسح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کے دلائل وہی ہیں جو مسح علی العمامۃ کے بارے میں گزرے ہیں (۲) ان چیزوں کے دھونے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور مسح کرنا دفع حرج کے لئے ہے اس لئے ہاتھ کو دھونا ہی ضروری ہوگا۔ دستانے پر مسح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لغت القفازين : دستانے
Ruling: Wiping over the turban, cap, burqa, and gloves is not permissible. (1) The verse commands wiping over the head, and it is not permissible to add to the Book of Allah through ahad hadith. Therefore, wiping over the turban, cap, and burqa is not allowed. In the ahadith mentioning that the Prophet wiped over his turban, the meaning is that he wiped part of his head and also over the turban. (2) Evidence: Anas ibn Malik said: I saw the Messenger of Allah performing wudoo, and he had a Qatari turban; he inserted his hand under the turban and wiped the front of his head, and did not undo the turban. (Abu Dawood). In Muslim: The Prophet wiped over his khuffs and the front of his head and over his turban. So this indicates he wiped part of the head and the turban. Therefore, wiping over only the turban is not sufficient. (3) Imam Tirmidhi said: The scholars say that wiping over just the turban is not sufficient unless one also wipes the head. This is the view of Sufyan al-Thawri, Malik ibn Anas, Ibn al-Mubarak, and al-Shafi'i. (4) Daraqutni dedicated a chapter on the permissibility of wiping over part of the head and cited four hadiths showing that wiping the head along with the turban is necessary. Similarly, wiping over gloves is not permissible. The proof for that is the same as for the turban. Also, there is no hardship in washing these items, and wiping is meant to dispel hardship, so washing the hands is necessary. Wiping over gloves is not allowed. Vocabulary: al-qafazain: gloves.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that wiping over head coverings (turban, cap, burqa) and hand coverings (gloves) during wudoo is not permissible in the Hanafi school. The author provides the evidence: the Quranic command in Surah al-Ma'idah (5:6) to wipe the head (wa islahu bi ru'usikum) is a general obligation that cannot be overridden by ahad hadiths that mention wiping over the turban. The ahadith reported are understood to mean that the Prophet wiped part of his head and also passed his hand over the turban, not that he wiped solely the turban. Authentic hadiths from Abu Dawood and Muslim show this method, where he inserted his hand under the turban to wipe his head. The scholars, including the Imams of the other schools, affirm that wiping over just the turban is insufficient. Similarly, for gloves: there is no hardship in washing the hands, so wiping is not a substitute. The general principle is that wiping over a barrier is allowed only when removing the barrier is difficult (like bandages), but turbans and gloves are easily removed, so the original obligation remains.

Key Terms
عمامة (imamah): Turban, a head wrap.
قلنسوة (qalansuwah): Cap or skullcap worn under the turban or alone.
قفازين (qafazayn): Pair of gloves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is wiping over a cap or turban alone not sufficient in wudoo?
A) Because the Quran commands wiping the head directly, and ahad hadith cannot override a definitive command.
B) Because turbans are usually dirty.
C) Because the Prophet never wiped over a turban.
D) Because the companions disagreed on this issue.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a removable head or hand covering does not fulfill the obligation of direct contact required in wudoo.

Wiping Over Bandages (Jaba'ir): Permissibility and Evidence
States that wiping over bandages is permissible even if tied without wudoo

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over bandages and identify the proof from the hadith of Ali.

Core Idea
Wiping over bandages is valid even if applied without wudoo — necessity overrides the general requirement of purity.

This passage addresses a common medical scenario: a person has a wound or fracture that is bandaged, and they need to perform wudoo or ghusl. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that wiping over the bandage suffices, and it does not matter whether the bandage was applied while the person was in a state of ritual purity. The evidence is drawn from explicit hadiths and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (wiping over bandages) and the classification of the ruling (permissible, ja'iz).
The ruling is a concession (rukhsah) due to hardship.
2
Recognize the condition
Note that the permissibility does not depend on when the bandage was applied. It is valid even if applied without wudoo.
This distinguishes the Hanafi view from some other schools.
3
Locate the dalil
Identify the textual proofs: the hadith in Abu Dawood and the explicit hadith from Ali (RA) narrated by Daraqutni and Ibn Majah.
The hadith of Ali directly addresses wiping over bandages in both wudoo and ghusl.
4
Extract the legal reasoning
Understand the underlying principle: removing the bandage involves hardship (haraj), so wiping over it is allowed.
This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) to alleviate difficulty.
5
Note the practice of the Companions
Observe that the Companions commonly applied bandages without wudoo and then wiped over them, confirming the ruling.
Their practice serves as tacit approval and evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسح جائز ہے زخم کی پٹیوں پر اگر چہ ان کو بغیر وضو کے باندھا ہو۔ (1) زخم کی پیٹیوں کو کھولنا مشکل ہے اور حرج ہے۔ اس لئے پٹی رہتے ہوئے اس پر مسح کیا جائے گا۔ چاہے پٹی کو حدث کی حالت میں باندھا ہو (۲) ابوداؤد میں یتعلیق ہے انما يكفيه ان يتيمم و يعصر او يعصب شک موسی على جرحه خرقه ثم يمسح عليها و يغسل سائر جسده (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی المجد در تیم ص ۵۵ نمبر ۳۳۶) (۳) عن علی بن طالب قال سألت رسول الله الله عن الجبائر يكون على الكسر كيف يتوضأ صاحبها وكيف يغتسل اذا اجنب؟ قال يمسحان بالماء عليها في الجنابة والوضوء (ج) (دارقطنی ، باب جواز امسح علی الجبائر ص۲۳۳نمبر ۸۶۵ر ابن ماجہ شریف، باب المسح علی الجبائر ص ۹۳، نمبر ۶۵۷ قی ، باب امسح على العصائب و الجبائر ج اول ص ۱۳۴۸ نمبر ۷ ۱۰۷) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ چینی پر مسح کرنا جائز ہے۔ والجبائر : جمع ہے جبیرة کی پٹی ، پیچی۔ نوت عمو مازخم پر بغیر وضو کے ہی پٹی باندھتے تھے اس کے باوجود صحابہ اس پر مسح کرتے تھے۔ کیونکہ مجبوری ہے۔ اس لئے بغیر وضو کے بھی پٹی باندھی جائے تو اس پر مسح جائز ہے۔
Ruling: Wiping is permissible over wound bandages, even if they were tied without wudoo. (1) Unwinding wound bandages is difficult and involves hardship. Therefore, wiping over the bandage is done while it is on, even if it was tied in a state of ritual impurity. (2) In Abu Dawood: It is sufficient for him to perform tayammum and then bandage (or squeeze?) his wound with a cloth, then wipe over it and wash the rest of his body. (3) Ali ibn Abi Talib said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about bandages on a fracture: how should the person perform wudoo and ghusl if he becomes junub? He replied: 'He should wipe over them with water in both ghusl and wudoo.' (Daraqutni, Ibn Majah). The hadith indicates that wiping over bandages is permissible. Vocabulary: al-jaba'ir is plural of jabirah, meaning bandage or splint. Note: In general, people often bandage wounds without wudoo, yet the Companions would wipe over them due to necessity. Therefore, even if the bandage was applied while not in wudoo, wiping over it is allowed.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding wiping over medical bandages (jaba'ir). The Hanafi position is that it is permissible to wipe over bandages during wudoo and ghusl, and it is valid even if the bandage was applied while the person was in a state of hadath (ritual impurity). The reason is that removing the bandage would cause hardship (haraj) and potentially harm the wound. The evidence comes from two hadiths: one in Abu Dawood about a person who bandages his wound and then wipes over it, and the clear hadith from Ali (RA) where the Prophet explicitly instructed to wipe over the bandage with water in both wudoo and ghusl. The author notes that the Companions often applied bandages without prior wudoo, yet they wiped over them out of necessity. Therefore, the permissibility remains regardless of when the bandage was applied. This ruling is an application of the principle of istihsan (juristic preference) to alleviate hardship.

Key Terms
جبائر (jaba'ir): Plural of jabirah: bandages, splints, or medical dressings applied to wounds or fractures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can a person wipe over a wound bandage during wudoo if the bandage was applied while they were not in a state of wudoo?
A) Yes, because hardship is the basis for the concession.
B) No, because the bandage was applied in impurity.
C) Only if the wound is bleeding.
D) Only if the bandage is made of cotton.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over bandages is a valid substitute for washing, regardless of when the bandage was applied, based on the hadith of Ali (RA) and the principle of necessity.

Wiping Over Headgear and Gloves in Wudu
Ruling on wiping over headgear and gloves with proof from hadith and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over a turban and gloves, and explain the proof from hadith and scholarly consensus.

Core Idea
Wiping a turban alone is insufficient; the head must be wiped, and gloves cannot be wiped.

Wiping over head coverings like turbans and caps is a common area of confusion. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: mere wiping over the turban does not fulfill the obligation of wiping the head. We will examine the hadith evidence and scholarly consensus, as well as the distinct ruling for gloves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Identify the act (wiping over turban/gloves) and the hukm (permissible or not).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Note the hadith from Anas ibn Malik and the additional report in Muslim.
The hadith show the Prophet wiped his forehead under the turban, not over it.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does the hadith prove the ruling? Focus on the phrase 'he inserted his hand under the turban' – this indicates direct contact with the head is required.
4
Note the scholarly consensus
The author cites Tirmidhi and Daraqutni to show that the majority of scholars, including the four imams, agree that wiping the head is necessary alongside the turban.
5
Apply to gloves
Why are gloves treated differently? The author explains that there is no difficulty in removing gloves, so the original obligation of washing the hands applies; wiping is not allowed.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاول ۸۳ كتاب الطهارة على العمامة والقلنسوة والبرقع والقفازين [۹۵] (۱۳) ويجوز على الجبائر وان شدها كہ سر کے بعض حصہ پر مسح کیا اور پگڑی پر بھی کر لیا (۲) چنانچہ حدیث میں اس طریقہ کار کا ثبوت ہے عن انس بن مالك قال رأيت
1
رسول الله له يتوضأ وعليه عمامة قطرية فادخل يده من تحت العمامة فمسح مقدم رأسه فلم ينقض العمامة (الف) ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب اسح علی العمامت ۶۱ نمبر ۱۴۷) مسلم میں ہے ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مسح على الخفين ومقدم رأسه وعلى عمامته ( مسلم شریف، باب امسح علیا لناصية والعمامة، ص ۱۳۴ نمبر ۲۷۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بعض سر پر مسح کیا اور پگڑی پر مسح کیا۔ اس لئے صرف پگڑی پر مسح کافی نہیں ہے (۳) امام ترمندی نے فرمایا کہ علماء فرماتے ہیں کہ صرف عمامہ پر مسح کرنا کافی نہیں ہو گا جب تک اس کے ساتھ سر پر بھی صبح نہ کر لے۔ وحوقول سفیان الثوری و مالک بن انس و ابن المبارک، والشافعی ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی امسح علی الجوربین والعمامۃ ص ۲۹نمبر۱۰۰) (۴) دار قطنی نے با ضابطہ باب باندھا ہے باب فی جواز امسح على بعض الرأس ( ج اول ص ۲۰ نمبر (۷۲) اور اس کے تحت ایسی چار حدیثیں ذکر کی ہیں جس سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ عمامہ کے ساتھ سر پر مسح کرنا ضروری ہے۔ دستانے پر بھی مسح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کے دلائل وہی ہیں جو مسح علی العمامۃ کے بارے میں گزرے ہیں (۲) ان چیزوں کے دھونے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور مسح کرنا دفع حرج کے لئے ہے اس لئے ہاتھ کو دھونا ہی ضروری ہوگا۔ دستانے پر مسح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 1, page 83, Book of Purification. On the turban, cap, burqa, and gloves [95] (13) And it is permissible on bandages, and if he tied them [explanation in Urdu: that he wiped on part of his head and also on the turban (2) and thus the proof of this method is in the hadith: from Anas ibn Malik who said: I saw the Messenger of Allah performing wudu while he had a Qatari turban, so he inserted his hand under the turban and wiped his forehead and did not unwrap the turban. (from Abu Dawud) And in Muslim: that the Prophet wiped over the khuffs and his forehead and over his turban. From this hadith it is understood that he wiped on part of the head and wiped on the turban. Therefore, wiping only on the turban is not sufficient. (3) Imam Tirmidhi said: The scholars say that wiping only on the turban is not sufficient unless one also wipes on the head along with it. This is the view of Sufyan al-Thawri, Malik ibn Anas, Ibn al-Mubarak, and al-Shafi'i. (4) Al-Daraqutni dedicated a chapter: Chapter on the permissibility of wiping on part of the head, and under it he mentioned four hadiths indicating that it is necessary to wipe the head along with the turban. Wiping on gloves is also not permissible. The proofs for this are the same as those mentioned for wiping on the turban. There is no difficulty in washing these items, and wiping is only to remove difficulty, therefore it is necessary to wash the hands. Wiping on gloves is not permissible.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof on wiping over head coverings and gloves during wudu. The author begins by stating the general rule about the turban, cap, burqa, and gloves, then provides proofs from hadith and scholarly consensus. The key ruling is that wiping over a turban alone is not sufficient; some part of the head must also be wiped. This is proven by the hadith of Anas ibn Malik, where the Prophet inserted his hand under the turban to wipe his forehead, and by the hadith in Muslim where the Prophet wiped over his khuffs, his forehead, and his turban. Imam Tirmidhi reports the consensus of scholars, including Sufyan al-Thawri, Malik, Ibn al-Mubarak, and al-Shafi'i, that wiping only on the turban is not enough. Al-Daraqutni also supports this with a chapter and four hadiths. As for gloves, the ruling is that wiping over them is not permissible because there is no difficulty in removing them; the hands must be washed. The proofs for gloves are the same as for the turban. This lesson establishes the Hanafi position that wiping over headgear requires direct contact with the head unless there is a valid excuse.

Key Terms
عمامة ('imamah): A turban worn on the head
قفازين (quffazayn): Gloves (dual form)
مسح (mash): Wiping with wet hand over a limb or covering

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, is it sufficient to wipe only over the turban during wudu?
A) Yes, because the turban covers the head
B) No, because the sunnah shows that the head must be wiped as well
C) Yes, if the turban is thick
D) No, only the head must be wiped, the turban is irrelevant

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, wiping over a turban alone does not fulfill the obligation of wiping the head; direct contact with the head is required, and gloves may not be wiped at all.

Ruling on Wiping over Bandages (Jaba'ir) and Its Effect on Wudu
Explains the permissibility of wiping over bandages and the effect of the bandage falling off

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over bandages, identify the conditions for its validity, and apply the distinction between the bandage falling off before and after healing.

Core Idea
Wiping over bandages is a concession valid only as long as the wound has not healed.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: a person has a wound or fracture covered by a bandage or splint (jabbirah). In such cases, the Hanafi school permits wiping over the bandage instead of washing the affected part, due to hardship. However, this concession is temporary. We will examine the proofs from the Sunnah and the crucial distinction: what happens if the bandage falls off before the wound heals versus after it heals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over bandages. The ruling is that it is permissible (rukhsah). This is established by the hadith of Ali ibn Abi Talib.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths are cited: one from Abu Dawud about wrapping and wiping, and one from Ali directly asking about bandages on a fracture. The command 'يمسحان بالماء عليها' indicates sufficiency.
The hadith from Ali is explicit and is the primary proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'يمسحان' (he should wipe) shows that wiping over the bandage is sufficient for both wudu and ghusl. This is a concession for hardship.
In Hanafi usul, the imperative indicates obligation, but here it is interpreted as a concession due to context.
4
Analyze the sub-rulings on bandage falling off
The passage gives two scenarios: if the bandage falls before healing, the wudu remains valid; if it falls after healing, the wudu is invalidated and the part must be washed.
This distinction hinges on the continuation of hardship.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The concession (rukhsah) applies only as long as the hardship (حرج) exists. Once the wound heals, the original ruling (washing) returns.
This principle is summarized in the text: 'One acts on the exceptional ruling only during hardship.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لغت القفازين : دستانے (۹۵) (۱۳) مسح جائز ہے زخم کی پٹیوں پر اگر چہ ان کو بغیر وضو کے باندھا ہو۔ (1) زخم کی پیٹیوں کو کھولنا مشکل ہے اور حرج ہے۔ اس لئے پٹی رہتے ہوئے اس پر مسح کیا جائے گا۔ چاہے پٹی کو حدث کی حالت میں باندھا ہو (۲) ابوداؤد میں یتعلیق ہے انما يكفيه ان يتيمم و يعصر او يعصب شک موسی على جرحه خرقه ثم يمسح عليها و يغسل سائر جسده (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی المجد در تیم ص ۵۵ نمبر ۳۳۶) (۳) عن علی بن طالب قال سألت رسول الله الله عن الجبائر يكون على الكسر كيف يتوضأ صاحبها وكيف يغتسل اذا اجنب؟ قال يمسحان بالماء عليها في الجنابة والوضوء (ج) (دارقطنی ، باب جواز امسح علی الجبائر ص۲۳۳نمبر ۸۶۵ر ابن ماجہ شریف، باب المسح علی الجبائر ص ۹۳، نمبر ۶۵۷ قی ، باب امسح على العصائب و الجبائر ج اول ص ۱۳۴۸ نمبر ۷ ۱۰۷) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ چینی پر مسح کرنا جائز ہے۔
السنن
الجبائر : جمع ہے جبیرة کی پٹی ، پیچی۔ نوت عمو مازخم پر بغیر وضو کے ہی پٹی باندھتے تھے اس کے باوجود صحابہ اس پر مسح کرتے تھے۔ کیونکہ مجبوری ہے۔ اس لئے بغیر وضو کے بھی پٹی
حاشیہ : (الف) میں نے حضور گو دیکھا کہ آپ کے سر پر قطری پگڑی تھی پس آپ نے پگڑی کے نیچے ہاتھ داخل کیا پھر سر کے اگلے حصہ پر مسح فرمایا اور پگڑی نہیں کھولی (ب) صرف اس کو کافی یہ ہوگا کہ تمیم کرے اور پٹی باندھے اپنے زخم پر موسی کو شک ہوا کی بعصر کہا یا عصب کہا۔ پھر اس پر مسح کرے اور باقی جسم کو دھوئے (ج) حضرت علی فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے حضور کو ٹوٹے ہوئے پر پچھی ہو اس کے بارے میں پوچھا کہ وہ کیسے وضو کرے اور جنبی ہو جائے تو کیسے غسل کرے؟ آپ نے فرمایا کہ دونوں پٹی پر پانی سے مسح کرے جنابت میں بھی اور وضو میں بھی۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاول ۸۴ كتاب الطهارة على غير وضوء [۱۴۹۶) فان سقطت من غير برء لم يبطل المسح ۹۷] (۱۵)
وانسقطت عن برء بطل.
باندھی تو اس پر سح کرنا جائز ہے۔
[۹۶] (۱۴) پس اگر بغیر زخم اچھا ہوئے پٹی گر گئی تو مسح باطل نہیں ہوگا۔
وضو کر کے پٹی پر مسح کیا تھا اس درمیان ابھی زخم ٹھیک نہیں ہوا تھا کہ پٹی گر گئی تو پہلا سے چلے گا۔ دوبارہ مسح کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں۔ جب تک زخم ٹھیک نہیں ہوا ہے تو پٹی باندھنا گویا کہ اس کو دھونا ہے اس لئے اس کو دوبارہ مسح کی ضرورت نہیں (۲) مجبوری بھی ہے۔ ۹۷ (۱۵) اگر کچھی زخم ٹھیک ہوکر گری ہو تو مسح باطل ہو جائے گا۔
زخم ٹھیک ہو گیا تو اب مجبوری نہیں رہی اس لئے اصل پر آ جائے گا اور مسح باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اب اس کو دوبارہ دھونا ہوگا۔
برء : زخم ٹھیک ہونا۔
مجبوری کے وقت ہی فرع پر عمل کہتا ہے اور مجری ختم ہو جائے تو اصل پرعمل کرناضروری ہے۔
Glossary of al-qaffazayn: gloves [95] (13) Wiping is permissible on wound bandages even if they were tied without wudu. (1) Opening the bandages of a wound is difficult and is a hardship. Therefore, as long as the bandage remains, wiping will be done over it, even if the bandage was tied in a state of hadath (ritual impurity). (2) In Abu Dawud it is related: 'It is sufficient for him to perform tayammum and to tightly wrap a cloth over his wound, then wipe over it, and wash the rest of his body.' (Abu Dawud, Book of Tayammum, no. 336) (3) From Ali ibn Abi Talib: He said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the bandages that are on a broken bone: How should the person perform wudu and how should he perform ghusl if he becomes junub? He said: 'He should wipe with water over them in both janabah and wudu.' (Al-Daraqutni, Ibn Majah, etc.) From the hadith it is known that wiping on bandages is permissible. Al-Sunnah. Al-Jaba'ir: plural of jabbirah: bandage, splint. It was common that they would tie bandages on wounds without wudu, yet the Companions would wipe over them because of necessity. Therefore, it is permissible even if the bandage was tied without wudu. Footnote (a): I saw the Prophet with a Qatari turban on his head; he inserted his hand under the turban then wiped his forehead and did not unwrap the turban. (b) It is sufficient for him to perform tayammum and to bandage his wound; Musa doubted whether he said 'ya'sir' or 'ya'sib'. Then he wipes over it and washes the rest of his body. (c) Ali said he asked the Prophet about a person with a splint on a fracture: How does he perform wudu and ghusl if junub? He said: 'He should wipe with water on them in janabah and wudu.' [PAGE_089] Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 1, page 84, Book of Purification. Without wudu [1496] If it falls off without healing, the wiping is not invalidated [97] (15) And if it falls off after healing, it is invalidated. He tied it, so wiping on it is permissible. [96] (14) So if the bandage falls off without the wound healing, the wiping is not invalidated. He performed wudu and wiped over the bandage; in the meantime, the wound had not yet healed when the bandage fell, so the previous (wudu) remains valid. There is no need to repeat the wiping. As long as the wound has not healed, tying the bandage is like washing it, so there is no need to repeat the wiping. (2) There is also hardship. (15) If the bandage falls after the wound has healed, then the wiping is invalidated. The wound has healed, so there is no longer hardship; therefore it returns to the original ruling and the wiping is invalidated. Now he must wash (that part) again. Bar' : healing of the wound. One acts on the exceptional ruling only during hardship; when the hardship ends, it is necessary to act on the original ruling.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof on wiping over bandages (jaba'ir) during wudu and ghusl. The author first explains that wiping over wound bandages is permissible even if the bandage was applied without a prior wudu, because removing the bandage causes hardship. This is supported by two hadiths: one from Abu Dawud that instructs to wrap a cloth over the wound and wipe over it while washing the rest of the body, and another from Ali ibn Abi Talib where the Prophet specifically allowed wiping over bandages for both wudu and ghusl when there is a fracture. The commentary then provides a glossary explaining that 'jaba'ir' refers to bandages or splints, and that the Companions would wipe over them due to necessity. The passage then addresses two sub-rulings: (14) if the bandage falls off before the wound heals, the initial wiping is not invalidated because the hardship remains; the person does not need to repeat the wudu or the wiping. (15) if the bandage falls off after the wound has healed, the wiping is invalidated because the hardship is gone, and the affected part must be washed in a fresh wudu. This distinction is based on the principle that exceptional rulings (like wiping over a bandage instead of washing) apply only for the duration of the hardship. Once the hardship ends, the original ruling (washing) is reinstated.

Key Terms
جبائر (jaba'ir): Plural of jabbirah; bandages, splints, or casts used for fractures or wounds
برء (bar'): Healing of a wound or fracture
مسح (mash): Wiping with wet hand over the bandage as a substitute for washing

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has a bandage on a wound, performs wudu by wiping over it, and then the bandage falls off before the wound heals, what is the ruling?
A) The wudu is invalidated and must be repeated
B) The wudu remains valid and no further action is needed
C) The bandage must be re-applied and the wiping repeated
D) The person must make ghusl

Key Takeaway
Wiping over bandages is a concession valid only as long as the wound remains unhealed; if the bandage falls after healing, the concession ends and the area must be washed.

Ruling on Bandage Falling Before Wound Heals
States ruling when a wound bandage falls prematurely

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a bandage falls before the wound heals and identify the condition of healing that determines whether masah remains valid or is invalidated.

Core Idea
Masah over a bandage remains valid if the bandage falls before the wound heals, but is invalidated if it falls after healing.

In the Hanafi school, wiping over a bandage (jabira) is a concession for those with wounds. This passage clarifies what happens if the bandage falls off prematurely. The key factor is whether the wound has healed. Understanding this ruling helps avoid unnecessary repetition of wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that masah over a bandage is a permissible concession during wudu when washing the wound would cause harm. This is a secondary ruling (rukhsah) due to necessity.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
The passage presents two possibilities: the bandage falls before the wound heals, or after the wound heals. The ruling differs based on this condition.
3
Determine the consequence
If the bandage falls before healing, the original masah remains valid—no need to re-wipe. If it falls after healing, the masah becomes invalid, and the area must be washed in subsequent wudu. The underlying reason is that the necessity (hardship) persists or ends.

Source Text

على غير وضوء فان سقطت من غير برء لم يبطل المسح وان سقطت عن برء بطل.
باندھی تو اس پر سح کرنا جائز ہے۔
[۹۶] (۱۴) پس اگر بغیر زخم اچھا ہوئے پٹی گر گئی تو مسح باطل نہیں ہوگا۔
وضو کر کے پٹی پر مسح کیا تھا اس درمیان ابھی زخم ٹھیک نہیں ہوا تھا کہ پٹی گر گئی تو پہلا سے چلے گا۔ دوبارہ مسح کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں۔ جب تک زخم ٹھیک نہیں ہوا ہے تو پٹی باندھنا گویا کہ اس کو دھونا ہے اس لئے اس کو دوبارہ مسح کی ضرورت نہیں (۲) مجبوری بھی ہے۔ ۹۷ (۱۵) اگر کچھی زخم ٹھیک ہوکر گری ہو تو مسح باطل ہو جائے گا۔
زخم ٹھیک ہو گیا تو اب مجبوری نہیں رہی اس لئے اصل پر آ جائے گا اور مسح باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اب اس کو دوبارہ دھونا ہوگا۔
برء : زخم ٹھیک ہونا۔
مجبوری کے وقت ہی فرع پر عمل کہتا ہے اور مجری ختم ہو جائے تو اصل پرعمل کرناضروری ہے۔
On without wudu: So if it falls without healing, the masah is not nullified, and if it falls after healing, it is nullified. Tying a bandage: so wiping over it is permissible. [96] (14) So if the bandage falls without the wound having healed, the masah will not be invalidated. He had performed wudu and wiped over the bandage; in the meantime, the wound had not yet healed and the bandage fell, so the previous [wudu] will suffice. There is no need to repeat the masah. As long as the wound has not healed, tying the bandage is like washing it, so there is no need to repeat the masah; also there is hardship. 97 (15) If the bandage falls after the wound has healed, then the masah becomes invalid. The wound healed, so there is no longer hardship; therefore it will revert to the original [ruling] and the masah becomes invalid. Now he will have to wash it again. Bar' : healing of the wound. Only at the time of hardship is the secondary [ruling] acted upon, and when the hardship ends, acting upon the original is necessary.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding the wiping over a bandage (jabira) on a wound. If the bandage falls off before the wound has healed, the masah remains valid—there is no need to repeat it. The reasoning is that the necessity (hardship) still exists, so the dispensation continues. However, if the bandage falls after the wound has completely healed, the masah is nullified because the necessity has ended. The person must then wash the area normally for subsequent wudu. The commentator explains that the bandage functions like a wash in the state of necessity; thus, re-wiping is not required while the wound remains unhealed. The term 'bar'' refers to the healing of the wound.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): Wiping over the bandage with wet hands instead of washing the wound area during wudu.
برء (bar'): Complete healing of the wound, removing the necessity that allowed masah.
جبرة (jabira): Bandage or splint applied to a wound or fracture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person wipes over a bandage during wudu, and the bandage falls off before the wound heals, what is the ruling?
A) The wudu is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The masah is invalid, but wudu remains valid.
C) The masah remains valid and no action is needed.
D) The person must wash the wound and repeat wudu.

Key Takeaway
The validity of masah over a bandage depends on the healing status of the wound.

Minimum and Maximum Duration of Hayd: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Defines hayd duration and presents inter-madhhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi minimum and maximum duration of hayd, identify the dalil, and compare the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
Hayd has fixed limits: 3 to 10 days; blood outside this range is istihadah.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on the duration of menstruation (hayd) and distinguishes it from chronic non-menstrual bleeding (istihadah). It then presents the differing views of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, along with their proofs. Understanding these limits is essential for determining obligations related to prayer, fasting, and marital relations.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: minimum 3 days and 3 nights, maximum 10 days. Any bleeding less or more is istihadah.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their views
Shafi'i: minimum 1 day, maximum 15 days. Maliki: no fixed minimum.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the hadith from Abu Umamah and Wathilah (Darqutni) that explicitly state the 3–10 day limit.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear and specific.
4
Analyze the opposing proofs
Shafi'i relies on the statement of 'Ata' (a tabi'i) stating min 1, max 15. Maliki relies on absence of explicit textual limit.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence: a woman with 1 day of bleeding does not treat it as hayd in the Hanafi school, but would in Shafi'i. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi due to stronger evidence.
The text itself advocates for the Hanafi view.

Source Text

نا امام شافعی کے نزدیک حیض کی کم سے کم مدت ایک دن ہے اور زیادہ سے زیادہ مدت پندرہ دن ہیں۔ ان کی دلیل یہ قول ہے عن عطاء قال اكثر الحيض خمسة عشرة وقال ادنى الحيض يوم (د) (دار قطنی، کتاب الحیض ص ۲۱۶ نمبر ۷۹۰٫۷۸۹ ) اس قسم کے قول سے وہ استدلال کرتے ہیں کہ حیض کی کم سے کم مدت ایک دن اور زیادہ سے زیادہ پندرہ دن ہیں۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک حیض کی کم سے کم مدت میں کوئی حدتعین نہیں ہے۔ کیوں کہ اوپر حضرت عطاء کا قول آیا کہ کم سے کم مدت ایک دن ہو سکتی ہے۔

Chapter of Menstruation. [9] (1) The minimum of hayd is three days and their nights, and what is less than that is not hayd but istihadah. Chapter of Menstruation: 'Hayd' linguistically means flowing. In Shari'ah, if blood exits from the womb of a woman who is not a minor, not past menopause, does not have the illness of continuous blood flow, and is not pregnant, then it is called hayd. If a woman has the illness of continuous blood flow, or is pregnant, or is a minor, or is past menopause, then the blood that exits is not hayd but istihadah. Its proof is the verse: 'They ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation and do not approach them until they become pure.' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:222). (98) (1) The minimum duration of hayd is three days and three nights, so what is less than that is not hayd but istihadah. And its maximum duration is ten days, and what exceeds that is istihadah. Blood that comes for less than three days and three nights is called blood of istihadah, not blood of hayd. Similarly, blood that exceeds ten days is also called blood of istihadah. The proof of this is the hadith from Abu Umamah al-Bahili: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Hayd does not occur for a young girl or an older woman who has reached menopause, less than three days or more than ten days. So if she sees blood beyond ten days, she is a mustahadah. Whatever exceeds her usual days, she makes up [the prayers]. The blood of hayd is deep black, with a reddish tinge, while the blood of istihadah is thin and yellowish.' And from Wathilah ibn al-Asqa' that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Indeed, the minimum of hayd is three days and its maximum is ten days.' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hayd, p. 25, no. 836/834). In Darqutni, there are several such hadiths indicating that the minimum is three days and the maximum ten. According to Imam Shafi'i, the minimum of hayd is one day and the maximum is fifteen days. Their proof is the statement of 'Ata': 'The maximum of hayd is fifteen days and the minimum is one day' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hayd, p. 216, no. 790/789). From such statements, they deduce that the minimum is one day and maximum fifteen. According to Imam Malik, there is no fixed minimum for hayd, because the statement of 'Ata' above indicates it could be one day. Footnotes: (a) [Quranic verse] (b) Hadith describing characteristics (c) Hadith stating min 3 max 10 (d) 'Ata' said max 15 min 1.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on hayd (menstruation) and establishes the Hanafi position on its minimum and maximum duration. It first defines hayd linguistically and legally, specifying that it applies to blood from the womb under normal conditions (not minor, not menopausal, not pregnant, not ill). The text then states the core ruling: the minimum duration is three full days and nights; any less is istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding). The maximum is ten days; beyond that is istihadah. Proofs are provided from the Quran (referring to menstruation as 'harm') and hadith from Abu Umamah and Wathilah. Then the passage presents the opposing views: Imam Shafi'i holds the minimum is one day and maximum fifteen, based on a statement from 'Ata'. Imam Malik holds no fixed minimum, also relying on 'Ata's statement and the absence of a clear textual limit. The Hadith quotes in the footnotes further describe the color of menstrual blood (black with reddish tinge) versus istihadah blood (thin and yellowish). This is an inter-madhhab dispute where the Hanafi school relies on specific prophetic hadith to set the limits, while other schools rely on general practice or statements of early scholars.

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Menstrual blood that flows from the womb of a woman who is not minor, menopausal, pregnant, or ill with continuous bleeding.
استحاضة (istihadah): Chronic non-menstrual bleeding that falls outside the defined limits of hayd, requiring different legal rulings.
اقل الحيض (aqqal al-hayd): The minimum duration of menstrual bleeding required for it to be considered hayd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One day
B) Three days and three nights
C) Ten days
D) Fifteen days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines hayd by duration: minimum 3 days, maximum 10; any bleeding outside this range is istihadah, not hayd.

Colors Considered Hayd and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains what color discharges count as hayd during menstrual days with evidence from Aisha and intra-Hanafi difference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which colors are considered hayd during menstrual days according to Abu Hanifa, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding kudrah.

Core Idea
During hayd days, every color except pure white is hayd; this is the Hanafi position based on Aisha's practice.

Have you ever wondered whether a yellowish or muddy discharge counts as menstruation? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on colored discharges during the days of hayd. We will examine the evidence from Aisha (رضي الله عنها), address an apparent contradiction with a statement from Umm Atiyyah, and then explore an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding muddy discharge (kudrah).

Guided Path
1
State the ruling from the matn
Identify the exact colors mentioned in the matn (redness, yellowness, muddiness) and the condition 'during hayd days'. Note the exception: pure white discharge (al-qissah al-bayda).
2
Analyze the evidence from Aisha
Examine the hadith where women sent cotton with yellow discharge to Aisha. She told them to wait until they see white discharge. Understand how this implies that any color before that is hayd.
This is the primary Hanafi dalil.
3
Reconcile with Umm Atiyyah's statement
Umm Atiyyah said 'We did not consider kudrah and sufrah as anything.' The text explains that this applies outside hayd days, not during. Distinguish between the two contexts.
This reconciliation is crucial to avoid confusion.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that kudrah (muddy) is not hayd even during hayd days. Understand his reasoning: it is due to diet, not menstrual blood. Note that Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa.
This is an ikhtilaf within the madhhab.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text indicates that Abu Hanifa's view (all colors except white are hayd) is the relied-upon position. Consider the strength of the evidence from Aisha.
For fatwa, this is the operative ruling.

[99] (2) Whatever a woman sees of redness, yellowness, and muddiness during the days of hayd, it is hayd, until she sees pure white. (2) And the woman during the time of hayd sees black blood, red blood, yellow, muddy, and green blood. Among these, white discharge is not hayd. But black, red, yellow, and muddy blood, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, will be considered hayd. Because the saying of Aisha: 'Other than pure white, all are hayd.' Women used to send to Aisha a vessel containing cotton with yellowness, and she would say: 'Do not be hasty until you see the white discharge (qissah bayda), meaning thereby purification from hayd.' (a) (Bukhari, Bab Iqbal al-Hayd, p. 46, no. 320). From this athar it is understood that during the days of hayd, until white discharge appears, all other colors are hayd. Umm Atiyyah narrated: 'We did not consider muddiness and yellowness as anything.' (b) (Bukhari, Bab al-Sufrah wal-Kudrah fi Ghayr Ayyam al-Hayd, p. 47, no. 326). In this saying, outside the days of hayd, muddy and yellow blood are not considered hayd. During the days of hayd, muddy and yellow blood will be considered hayd, as understood from Aisha's saying. Now Imam Abu Yusuf says: Muddy blood is not hayd. It is due to dietary imbalance, not part of menstrual blood. His evidence is the saying of Umm Atiyyah: 'We did not consider muddiness and yellowness as anything.' (Bukhari, no. 326). If a woman is menstruating, green blood is hayd; if she is menopausal, green blood is istihadah. Lexicon: al-sufrah: yellow color; al-kudrah: muddy color. Footnote: (a) Explanation of Aisha's practice. (b) Umm Atiyyah's statement: we did not count kudrah and sufrah as anything.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage addresses the colors of discharge that count as menstruation (hayd) during the days a woman is menstruating. The matn states that any redness, yellowness, or muddiness (kudrah) seen during hayd days is hayd until pure white discharge (al-qissah al-bayda) appears. The commentary explains that Imam Abu Hanifa includes all colors except white: black, red, yellow, muddy, and even green (for a menstruating woman) are hayd. The evidence is the practice of Aisha, who would tell women not to consider themselves pure until they saw white discharge. This indicates that any colored discharge during hayd days is part of hayd. The commentary then presents a narration from Umm Atiyyah that women did not consider kudrah and sufrah as anything (i.e., not hayd), but the scholar clarifies that this applies outside hayd days, not during. Then an intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that muddy discharge (kudrah) is not hayd because it results from dietary issues, citing Umm Atiyyah's general statement. The passage concludes with a lexical note and footnotes. The author follows the order: matn, then explanation integrating proofs and dispute. The Hanafi position is that all colors except pure white are hayd during hayd days, and this is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
صفرة (sufrah): Yellow-colored discharge; considered hayd during menstrual days according to Abu Hanifa.
كدرة (kudrah): Muddy or dull-colored discharge; considered hayd by Abu Hanifa, not by Abu Yusuf.
قصة بيضاء (al-qissah al-bayda): Pure white discharge indicating the end of hayd and purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Red blood
B) Yellow discharge
C) Muddy discharge
D) Pure white discharge

Key Takeaway
During menstrual days, all colors except pure white are considered hayd according to Abu Hanifa, with muddy discharge being an intra-Hanafi point of contention.

Rulings of Hayd: Salat and Sawm
States that hayd drops salat obligation, forbids sawm, with qada for sawm only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat and sawm during hayd and explain the rationale for the difference.

Core Idea
Hayd drops salat entirely (no qada) but only delays sawm (qada required).

This passage presents a foundational ruling in fiqh al-hayd: the effect of menstruation on the two major acts of worship, salat and sawm. While both are obligatory under normal circumstances, hayd completely lifts the obligation of salat, while sawm is merely postponed. Understanding this distinction is essential for every Muslim woman's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their rulings
The passage explicitly states two rulings: (1) hayd 'drops' salat, meaning the obligation is removed entirely; (2) hayd makes sawm 'forbidden' during the days of menstruation, with a requirement to make it up later.
Focus on the verbs 'yasqutu' (drops) and 'yuharramu' (makes forbidden).
2
Determine the hukm level for each act
For salat: the original hukm is fard 'ayn, but hayd drops it completely, so there is no obligation during hayd and no qada. For sawm: the original fard obligation remains, but performance during hayd is haram; therefore qada is wajib after hayd ends.
The commentary highlights the rationale: hardship (haraj) in making up many prayers.
3
Examine the rationale for the difference
The passage explains that requiring qada of salat would cause immense hardship because a woman may miss up to 50 prayers per month. Sawm, being only once a year, does not pose such hardship.
This is a good example of the Hanafi principle of raf' al-haraj (removal of hardship).
4
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Consider a woman who menstruates for 7 days in Ramadan. She misses 35 prayers (5 per day) and 7 fasts. According to this ruling, she does not make up the prayers but must make up the 7 fasts after Ramadan.
This clarifies the practical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١٠٠] (۳) والحيض يسقط عن الحائض الصلوة ويحرم عليها الصوم وتقضى الصوم ولا تقضى [۱] (۳) حیض ساقط کر دیتا ہے حائضہ عورت سے نماز کو اور حرام کر دیا تا ہے اس پر روزہ ۔ چنانچہ حائضہ قضا کرے گی روزہ اور نہیں قضا کرے گی نماز کو۔ تشریح حیض کی حالت میں نماز شروع ہی سے ساقط ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے بعد میں اس کی قضا نہیں ہے۔ اور روزہ واجب ہوتا ہے لیکن حیض کی حالت میں اس کو ادا نہیں کرسکتی۔ اس کا ادا کر ناحرام ہے اس لئے بعد میں قضا کرے گی (۱) دس روز کی نمازیں پچاس ہو جائینگی اور ہر ماہ میں پچاس نمازیں قضا کرنے میں حرج عظیم ہے اس لئے نماز شروع ہی سے ساقط ہو
[100] (3) And hayd drops salat from the menstruating woman, and makes sawm forbidden upon her. She makes up the sawm but does not make up the salat. (3) Hayd drops salat from the menstruating woman and forbids sawm on her. So the menstruating woman will make up sawm and will not make up salat. Explanation: During hayd, salat is dropped from the beginning, so there is no qada for it afterwards. Sawm is obligatory but during hayd she cannot perform it; performing it is forbidden, so she will make it up later. (1) Ten days of salat become fifty (for five daily prayers) and making up fifty prayers every month would be an immense hardship, so salat is dropped from the start.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents a concise ruling (hukm) about the effect of menstruation (hayd) on prayer (salat) and fasting (sawm). It states two effects: first, hayd completely drops the obligation of salat from the menstruating woman, and she does not need to make up those prayers after her hayd ends. Second, hayd makes sawm forbidden during the days of menstruation, but she must make up those missed fasts later. The commentary (sharh) explains the rationale: salat is dropped entirely because requiring the qada of multiple prayers (e.g., 10 days of all five prayers would be 50 prayers each month) would cause great hardship (haraj). Therefore, the obligation is lifted from the beginning, and no compensation is required. In contrast, sawm is only delayed; it remains obligatory (wajib) but cannot be performed during hayd, so it must be made up after purity. This distinction is based on the frequency of the acts: salat is daily and multiple, sawm is once a year in Ramadan. The Hanafi school emphasizes the 'haraj' principle for dropping salat qada. The passage does not provide a specific Quranic or hadith proof, but the ruling is established by ijma and the principle of ease. This is a fundamental rule in fiqh al-hayd.

Key Terms
يسقط (yasqutu): To fall away or be dropped; here it means the obligation of salat is removed due to hayd.
قضاء (qada): Making up an obligatory act after its prescribed time; here for sawm only.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a menstruating woman make up after her hayd ends?
A) Both salat and sawm
B) Salat only
C) Sawm only
D) Neither salat nor sawm

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, hayd completely drops the obligation of salat (no qada) but only delays sawm (qada required), based on the principle of removing hardship.

Menstruating Woman: Prohibition from Mosque and Tawaf
Ruling for menstruating women regarding mosque entry and tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a menstruating woman entering a mosque and performing tawaf, and identify the prophetic proofs (dalil) that establish the prohibition.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman is forbidden from entering any mosque and from performing tawaf until she is pure, based on explicit hadith.

This lesson examines two prohibitions that apply to a woman during her menstrual period (hayd): entering a mosque and performing tawaf around the Kaaba. These rulings are derived from clear prophetic commands and are unanimously held in the Hanafi school, though some other schools allow entry under certain conditions. Understanding these prohibitions is essential for a menstruating woman to observe her religious duties correctly during Hajj and in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The text explicitly states two prohibitions: a menstruating woman must not enter a mosque and must not perform tawaf. Note that these are separate rulings with separate proofs.
2
Locate the dalil for each
The author cites two hadith: one from Abu Dawud (general prohibition of mosque entry for menstruating and junub) and one from Bukhari (specific prohibition of tawaf during Hajj). Identify each dalil and its source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each hadith prove the ruling? The first uses the explicit phrase 'I do not permit' (la ahillu), indicating absolute prohibition. The second uses the command 'do not perform tawaf until you become pure', implying tawaf is invalid without purification.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) permit a menstruating woman to enter a mosque for necessity or in a state of covering. The Hanafi school strictly prohibits it. Understand the practical difference.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the literal implication of the hadith and is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling in the school. The authority is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴) ولا تدخل المسجد ولا تطوف بالبيت
(۱) حدیث میں ہے کہ سمعت عائشة ... فقال وجهوا هذه البيوت عن المسجد فاني لا احل المسجد لحائض ولا جنب ( ب ) ( ابوداؤد و شریف، باب فی الجنب يدخل المسجد ص ۳۴ نمبر ۲۳۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حائضہ عورت مسجد میں داخل نہیں ہوسکتی ۔ اور مسجد حرام میں طواف ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ طواف بھی نہیں کر سکتی (۲) تاہم طواف کے منع کے بارے میں مستقل حدیث ہے عن عائشة قال لعلك نفست؟ قلت نعم قال فان ذالک شیء كتبه الله على بنات آدم فافعل ما يفعل الحاج غير لا تطوفى بالبيت حتى تطهری (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب تقضی الحائض المناسک کلھا الا الطواف بالبیت ص ۴۴ نمبر (۳۰۵) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حائضہ عورت طواف نہیں کرے گی۔
(4) And she must not enter the mosque nor perform tawaf around the House. (1) In a hadith: I heard Aisha... she said: 'Turn these houses away from the mosque, for I do not permit the mosque for a menstruating woman nor for a junub.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on junub entering mosque, p.34 no.232). From this hadith it is understood that a menstruating woman cannot enter the mosque. And tawaf occurs in the Sacred Mosque, therefore she also cannot perform tawaf. (2) However, there is a specific hadith forbidding tawaf: from Aisha: He said: 'Perhaps you are menstruating?' I said: 'Yes.' He said: 'That is a thing Allah has written upon the daughters of Adam. So do what the pilgrim does, except do not perform tawaf around the House until you become pure.' (Bukhari, chapter on menstruating woman performs all rites except tawaf, p.44 no.305). From this hadith it is understood that a menstruating woman will not perform tawaf.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage states two prohibitions for a menstruating woman: entering a mosque and performing tawaf around the Kaaba. The author provides two proofs: first, a hadith from Aisha where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered that dwellings be directed away from the mosque, declaring it impermissible for a menstruating woman and a junub. Second, a hadith from Aisha during Hajj: the Prophet instructed her to do all acts of pilgrimage except tawaf until she is pure. This establishes that menstruation does not prevent other rites, only tawaf. The prohibition of entering the mosque is based on impurity, and tawaf is a form of worship that requires purity.

Key Terms
حائض (ha'id): A woman experiencing menstrual bleeding.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba, a pillar of Hajj/Umrah.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major impurity (janabah) requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She can perform tawaf if she wears gloves.
B) She is prohibited from tawaf until she becomes pure.
C) She must perform tawaf and repeat it later.
D) She can perform tawaf but must not recite Quran.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman is prohibited from entering any mosque and from performing tawaf until she becomes pure, based on explicit hadith; other Hajj rites are permitted.
