كتاب الطهارة
تراه الحامل وما تراه المرأة فى حال ولادتها قبل خروج الولد استحاضة [١١](١٩) واقل النفاس لا حد له واكثره اربعون يوما ومازاد على ذلك فهو استحاضة (٢٠) واذا تجاوز الدم على الاربعين وقد كانت هذه المرأة ولدت قبل ذلك
ولها عادة فى النفاس ردت الى ايام عادتها وان لم يكن لها عادة فنفاسها اربعون يوما خالی رحم سے نکلتا ہے اور یہاں رحم بچہ سے بھرا ہوا ہے (۲) حیض کی جھلیاں کٹ کٹ کر اگرتی ہیں تو حیض ہوتا ہے اور بچہ کی حالت میں بچہ کا آنول جھلیوں کے ساتھ چپکا ہوتا ہے اس لئے جھلیاں نہیں کٹ سکے گی اس لئے وہ حیض کا خون نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح بچہ کی وجہ سے رحم کا منہ بند ہے اس لئے نہ حیض آسکتا ہے اور نہ نفاس۔ اس لئے وہ استحاضہ کا خون ہے۔
با امام شافعی اس کو حیض قرار دیتے ہیں ام (۱۹) نفاس کی کم سے کم مدت کے لئے کوئی حد نہیں ہے اور اس کی زیادہ مدت چالیس دن ہیں اور جو اس سے زیادہ ہو وہ استحاضہ ہے۔
صلى الله
حدیث میں ہے عن ام سلمة قالت كانت النفساء تجلس على عهد رسول الله له اربعين يوما (الف) (ترندى
شریف، باب ماجاء فی کم تمکٹ النفساء ص ۳۵ نمبر ۱۳۹) اور ابو داؤد شریف کی روایت میں یہ جملہ زیادہ ہے۔ لا يأمرها النبي بقضاء صلواة النفاس (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء فی وقت النفسا ص ۴۹ نمبر ۳۱۲) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نفاس کی زیادہ سے زیادہ مدت چالیس دن ہے۔ اس کے بعد جو خون آئے گا وہ استحاضہ ہوگا۔ اور کم کی کوئی حد نہیں ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن انس قال قال رسول الله الا الله وقت النفاس اربعون يوما الا ان ترى الطهر قبل ذلك (ج) (دار قطنی، کتاب الحيض ، حدیث نمبر ۱ ۱۸۴ ترمذی شریف حدیث نمبر ۱۳۹) الا ان ترى الطهر قبل ذلک سے معلوم ہوا کہ چالیس دن سے پہلے خون بند ہو جائے یو چا ہے چند گھنٹے کے بعد خون بند ہو جائے عورت پاک ہو جائے گی۔
[۱۱۷) (۲۰) نفاس کا خون چالیس دن سے تجاوز کر جائے حالانکہ یہ عورت اس سے پہلے بچہ جن چکی تھی اور اس کے لئے نفاس میں عادت تھی تو نفاس کا خون لوٹا یا جائے گا اس کی عادت کی طرف۔ اور اگر اس کی عادت نہ ہو تو اس کے نفاس کی مدت چالیس دن ہے۔
تشریح جس عورت کو پہلے بچہ پیدا ہو چکا ہو اور نفاس کے لئے اس کی ایک عادت ہو مثلا پچیس روز نفاس آتا ہواب اس کو پچاس روز تک خون آ گیا تو دس روز تو یقیناً استحاضہ ہے اس لئے اس دس روز کے ساتھ باقی پندرہ دن بھی استحاضہ شمار کیا جائے گا۔ اور اس کی پہلی عادت کے مطابق چھپیں روز ہی نفاس ہوگا۔ کیونکہ چالیس دن کے بعد والے دس دن استحاضہ ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ چھپیں دن کے بعد بھی استحاضہ ہی آیا ہے۔ اور اگر اس عورت کی کوئی عادت نہیں ہے تو حدیث کے مطابق چالیس روز نفاس ہوگا اور باقی دن استحاضہ ہو گا۔ عادت کی طرف پھیرنے کی دلیل تو ہوگا
حاشیہ : (ب) ام سلمہ فرماتی ہیں کہ نفساء عورت حضور کے زمانے میں چالیس دن تک بیٹھتی تھی (نماز نہیں پڑھتی تھی (ب ) حضور نفاس کے وقت کی نماز قضا کرنے کا حکم نہیں دیتے تھے (ج) حضور نے نفاس کا وقت چالیس دن متعین کیا۔ مگر یہ کہ اس سے پہلے طہر دیکھ لے تو پہلے بھی پاک ہو جائے گی)
And nifas is blood that emerges after childbirth. [...] A pregnant woman who sees blood, or a woman at the time of delivery before the child exits, that is istihadah. [...] The minimum of nifas has no limit, and its maximum is forty days, and what exceeds that is istihadah. [...] When the blood exceeds forty days, and this woman has previously given birth and has a habit in nifas, she returns to her habitual days; if she has no habit, then her nifas is forty days.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on nifas (postpartum bleeding) and its limits. It defines nifas as blood that emerges after childbirth, and clarifies that blood seen during pregnancy or during delivery before the baby exits is istihadah (chronic bleeding), not nifas or menses. The minimum duration of nifas has no lower limit — even if bleeding stops a few hours after birth, the woman becomes pure. The maximum is forty days based on the hadith from Umm Salamah that women in the Prophet's time would sit (refrain from prayer) for forty days, and the Prophet did not command them to make up missed prayers. If bleeding exceeds forty days, the woman who has a previous nifas habit (e.g., 25 days) returns to that habit, and the additional days are istihadah. If she has no habit, her nifas is set at forty days, and the rest is istihadah. This ruling is derived from the hadith of Anas (ra) that the Prophet set the time of nifas as forty days unless she sees purity before that. The commentary also notes that Imam al-Shafi'i considers blood during pregnancy as menses, but the Hanafi position is that it is istihadah.

Key Terms
نفاس (nifās): Blood that emerges after childbirth, whether the child is born alive or stillborn.
استحاضة (istiḥāḍah): Abnormal vaginal bleeding that is not part of menses or nifas; it occurs due to a cause (e.g., pregnancy, delivery before birth, or after 40 days).
عادة (ʿādah): A woman's established pattern (duration) of nifas from previous deliveries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling for a woman who has previously given birth and has a habit of 25 days of nifas, but this time bleeds for 50 days?
A) The entire 50 days is nifas.
B) The first 40 days are nifas, the remaining 10 days are istihadah.
C) She returns to her habit of 25 days of nifas, and the remaining 25 days are istihadah.
D) She must wait 40 days then take a bath.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on nifas is flexible: no minimum, maximum 40 days, and a prior habit can shorten the nifas period if bleeding exceeds 40 days; any bleeding beyond the habit or the 40-day default is istihadah.

Duration and Classification of Nifas
Ruling on duration of nifas and classification of antepartum blood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum and maximum duration of nifas and distinguish it from istihadah, citing the primary proofs.

Core Idea
Nifas has no minimum and a maximum of 40 days; blood before delivery is istihadah.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on post-natal bleeding (nifas). The school holds that nifas has no set minimum — even a few hours of bleeding after birth qualifies — and a maximum of forty days based on authentic hadith. We also address the classification of blood seen before the child's delivery, which the Hanafi school considers istihadah (invalid bleeding), contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i who considers it hayd. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying rulings of purity, prayer, and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on blood before delivery
Read the first sentence: what is the Hanafi classification of blood seen during pregnancy or before the child emerges?
The text explicitly says it is istihadah.
2
State the duration rulings for nifas
Find the statements on minimum and maximum: there is no lower limit, the upper limit is forty days.
The minimum is not defined — bleeding may stop immediately after birth.
3
Review the proofs for the maximum
Examine the hadith cited: from Umm Salamah and Anas. Note the exceptions ('unless she sees purity before that').
These are ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalala, but accepted as evidence.
4
Note the inter-madhhab difference
Identify that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees on the classification of pre-delivery blood.
The text only mentions the disagreement without providing Shafi'i's proof.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a woman who gives birth and bleeds for 30 days then stops, classify her state. If she bleeds for 45 days, what is the ruling?
The first is nifas, the second: after 40 days it becomes istihadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The blood seen by a pregnant woman and what the woman sees during her birth before the child comes out is istihadah. The minimum of nifas has no limit, its maximum is forty days, and what exceeds that is istihadah. Explanation: Blood coming from an empty womb is hayd or nifas, but here the womb is filled with the child. In menstruation, the membranes are cut, but in pregnancy the placenta is attached, so the membranes cannot be cut, thus it is not menstrual blood. Similarly, due to the child, the mouth of the womb is closed, so neither hayd nor nifas can occur, so it is istihadah. Imam Shafi'i considers it hayd. (19) There is no limit for the minimum of nifas, its maximum is forty days, and what exceeds that is istihadah. In a hadith from Umm Salamah: 'The woman in nifas used to sit (not pray) for forty days during the time of the Prophet.' In Abu Dawud: 'The Prophet did not command her to make up the prayers of nifas.' These hadith show the maximum is forty days. There is no limit for the minimum, evidence from Anas: 'The Prophet said nifas is forty days unless she sees purity before that.'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the classification of blood seen during pregnancy and after childbirth. It first states that any blood seen before the delivery of the child is istihadah (invalid bleeding), not nifas or hayd. The reason given is that the womb is occupied with the child, preventing the normal process of menstruation. The author then notes that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees and considers such blood to be hayd. Next, the ruling on the duration of nifas is given: there is no minimum period, and the maximum is forty days based on authentic hadith. Any blood beyond forty days is istihadah. The hadith of Umm Salamah and Anas are cited as proofs. The commentary emphasizes that even if blood stops a few hours after birth, the woman becomes pure immediately.

Key Terms
نفاس (nifas): Post-natal bleeding that occurs after the child is born, with a maximum of forty days.
استحاضة (istihadah): Bleeding that is not hayd or nifas, considered invalid bleeding that does not prevent prayer or fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 10 days
B) 30 days
C) 40 days
D) 60 days

Key Takeaway
Nifas has no minimum and a maximum of 40 days; any blood before delivery is istihadah.

Returning to Habit When Nifas Exceeds 40 Days
Ruling on nifas exceeding 40 days with habit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a woman whose nifas exceeds 40 days and apply the rule of habit to determine the nifas period.

Core Idea
Nifas is her habit if known; otherwise forty days – blood beyond is istihadah.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a woman's postnatal bleeding continues beyond the maximum forty days. The Hanafi school provides a clear rule based on her previous habit. If she has given birth before and knows her usual nifas length, she returns to that habit. If not, the full forty days are nifas. The difference affects her prayers and worship obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: the classification of bleeding after childbirth (nifas) when it exceeds 40 days.
The ruling is not a hukm taklifi but a legal determination of period.
2
State the Two Scenarios
The text provides two cases: (1) woman has a previous habit (adah) from earlier births; (2) she has no habit. State the ruling for each.
Habit means the number of days she previously experienced nifas, e.g., 25 days.
3
Examine the Dalil
The proof is the hadith of Umm Salamah that women in the Prophet's time would sit (not pray) for forty days. This establishes the maximum, allowing return to habit for shorter periods.
The hadith is ahad, so dalala is zanni.
4
Apply the Ruling to an Example
Work through the example in the commentary: a woman with a 25-day habit bleeds for 50 days. The first 25 are nifas, the remaining 25 are istihadah.
Blood beyond 40 is definitely istihadah; here the habit is within 40, so the extra beyond habit is istihadah.
5
Consider Practical Consequences
Understand that correct classification affects whether she performs salah, fasts, or has sexual relations. Only nifas days exempt her from prayer; istihadah days require prayer with wudu for each time.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if she mistakenly treated extra days as nifas, she would miss obligatory prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if the blood exceeds forty days, and this woman had given birth before and had a habit in nifas, she is returned to her habit days; if she had no habit, her nifas is forty days. Explanation: If the blood exceeds forty days and she had a previous habit, she is returned to that habit. If no habit, forty days. Example: if habit was 25 days, and blood comes for 50 days, the first 25 are nifas, the remaining 25 are istihadah. The proof is that after 40 days it is istihadah. The hadith of Umm Salamah is mentioned.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where a woman's nifas blood continues beyond forty days. If she has a previous habit (e.g., her last nifas was 25 days), then she reverts to that habit, and the extra days are considered istihadah. If she has no habit, the full forty days are counted as nifas. The example explains: a woman with a 25-day habit bleeds for 50 days; the first 20? Actually the text says 25? It says 'pachis roz' i.e., 25. So the first 25 are nifas, the next 25 are istihadah because they exceed 40? Wait, the example says 50 days total, so 25 habit, then 25 extra. But 40 days is the max, so 10 days beyond 40 are definitely istihadah, and the remaining 15 of the extra are also istihadah because they are beyond the habit. The commentary clarifies: the woman returns to her habit, and any blood beyond that (even within 40) is not nifas if it exceeds the habit? Actually, the hanafi position is that if she had a habit, the nifas period is her habit, even if less than 40. The text in the matn says she is returned to her habit days. So if habit is 25, only 25 are nifas. Then the remaining days up to 40? Actually the example: 50 days total, habit 25, so 25 nifas, then the remaining 25 are istihadah. That means blood beyond habit is istihadah, even if within 40. The text does not specify that the habit must be within 40; it assumes the habit is less than 40. If the habit was 45 days? That cannot happen because max is 40. So habit is always within 40.

Key Terms
عادة (adah): A woman's habitual duration of nifas from previous births.
نفاس (nifas): Postnatal bleeding; its maximum is 40 days in Hanafi unless habit is known.
استحاضة (istihadah): Non-menstrual bleeding that is not nifas; requires wudu for each prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman has a habit of 20 days of nifas, but her blood continues for 50 days, how many days are considered nifas?
A) 20 days
B) 40 days
C) 50 days
D) The first 20 days and the last 10?

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a woman's known habit of nifas overrides the forty-day maximum; blood beyond the habit, even within forty, is istihadah.

Nifas When Giving Birth to Twins
Intra-Hanafi dispute on when nifas begins for twins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on when nifas begins for twins and explain the reasoning of each side.

Core Idea
For twins, Abu Hanifa counts nifas from the first birth; Muhammad counts from the second—the dispute turns on whether the remaining pregnancy overrides the birth.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement about classifying blood after the birth of twins. While all agree that nifas is blood after childbirth, they differ on when 'childbirth' is considered complete. The dispute illustrates how different usul perspectives (focusing on delivery vs. ongoing pregnancy) lead to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What exactly is being disagreed upon? The start of nifas for a woman giving birth to twins.
2
State each position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: blood after the first child is nifas. Muhammad and Zufar: blood after the second child is nifas.
3
Analyze the dalil for each
Abu Hanifa: the first child is a complete birth, the womb opens, so blood is nifas. Muhammad: the second child remains in the womb, so she is still pregnant; blood during pregnancy is istihadah.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
If nifas starts after first, she observes nifas rulings from first bleeding; if after second, earlier blood is istihadah and she prays.
5
Consider the tarjih
The text does not specify which view is mufta bihi. Later Hanafi works may prefer Abu Hanifa's view.

ومن ولدت ولدين في بطن واحد فنفاسها ما خرج من الدم عقيب الولد الاول عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى وقال محمد و زفر رحمهما الله تعالى من الولد الثاني. اور حدیث مسئلہ نمبر 19 میں گزرگئی۔ [۱۱] (۲۱) کسی عورت نے ایک ہی حمل سے دو بچے دیے تو اس کا نفاس وہ خون ہے جو پہلے بچے کے بعد نکلے امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ۔ اور امام محمد اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ دوسرے بچے کے بعد ۔ امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک بچہ پیدا ہونے کے بعد رحم کا منہ کھل گیا اور انسان بھی پیدا ہو گیا جس سے لفظ نفاس مشتق ہے۔ اس لئے پہلے بچے کے بعد جو خون نکلے گا وہ سب نفاس شمار کیا جائے گا۔ اور امام محمد اور ز فر فر ماتے ہیں کہ ایک بچہ پیٹ میں موجود ہے اس لئے عورت ابھی حاملہ ہے اور حمل کی حالت میں جو خون آتا ہے وہ استحاضہ کا خون ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے پہلے بچے کے بعد جو خون ہے وہ استحاضہ کا خون ہوگا۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ ابھی رحم کا منہ بھی پورا کھلا ہوا نہیں ہے جب تک کہ دوسرا بچہ پیدا ہو کر منہ پورا نہ کھل جائے نفاس کا خون کیسے شمار کیا جائے گا۔ طرفین کی نظر بچہ پیدا ہونے کی طرف گئی اور امام محمد کی نظر اندر جو بچہ ابھی تک موجود ہے اس کی طرف گئی۔ بعد میں
And if she gives birth to two children in one belly, her nifas is the blood that comes out after the first child according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad and Zufar said: after the second child. Hadith passed in issue 19. (21) A woman gave birth to twins, her nifas is the blood that comes after the first child according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar said after the second. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf argue: after the first child the mouth of the womb opens and a human being is born, so blood after the first is nifas. Imam Muhammad and Zufar argue: the second child is still in the womb, so she is still pregnant, and blood during pregnancy is istihadah, so blood after the first is istihadah, and also the womb is not fully open until the second child is born.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the classification of blood after the birth of the first twin. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider the blood after the first birth as nifas because the child has been delivered and the womb has opened, fulfilling the definition of nifas. Muhammad and Zufar, however, argue that since a child remains in the womb, the woman is still in a state of pregnancy, and any blood during pregnancy is istihadah, not nifas. Additionally, the mouth of the womb is not fully open until both children are delivered. The disagreement stems from different perspectives: Abu Hanifa focuses on the birth of the first child, while Muhammad focuses on the remaining pregnancy. The mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated here, but later Hanafi works may favor Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
نفاس (nifas): Postnatal bleeding after childbirth; here disputed if it applies after first or second twin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, when does nifas begin for a woman giving birth to twins?
A) After the first child
B) After the second child
C) Forty days after the first child
D) Only if there is bleeding after both children

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the classification of blood after the first twin depends on whether one prioritizes the birth event (Abu Hanifa) or the ongoing pregnancy (Muhammad).

When Does Nifas Begin for Twin Births? An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nifas for twins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on nifas for twins and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
For twins, nifas begins after the first birth according to Abu Hanifa, but after the second according to Muhammad.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when does postpartum bleeding (nifas) start for a woman who gives birth to twins? The answer determines whether the blood between births is nifas (preventing prayer and other acts requiring purity) or istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding allowing prayer with wudu). The reasoning hinges on whether the remaining fetus makes the woman still pregnant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Determine which Hanafi imams hold which view. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: nifas begins after first child. Muhammad and Zufar: nifas begins after second child.
2
Analyze the evidence for each view
For Abu Hanifa: after first birth, womb opens and a human is delivered, which is the meaning of nifas. For Muhammad: the woman is still pregnant, so bleeding is istihadah; the womb is not fully open until the second birth.
Both sides use the same criterion (womb opening and delivery) but disagree on when it is fully realized.
3
Derive the practical consequence (thamarah)
Apply each view to a woman who bleeds between births. Under Abu Hanifa: she is in nifas and cannot pray. Under Muhammad: she is mustahada and may pray after wudu.
This is the operational difference.
4
Evaluate the reasoning (talil)
Note that the dispute is about the underlying cause (illah) of nifas: is it the mere delivery of any child, or is it the complete emptying of the womb?
This is a key usul exercise.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (if known)
The passage does not specify a relied-upon view. Later Hanafi preference often follows Abu Hanifa in zahir al-riwayah, but both are transmitted.

اور حدیث مسئلہ نمبر 19 میں گزرگئی۔
[۱۱] (۲۱) کسی عورت نے ایک ہی حمل سے دو بچے دیے تو اس کا نفاس وہ خون ہے جو پہلے بچے کے بعد نکلے امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ۔ اور امام محمد اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ دوسرے بچے کے بعد ۔
امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک بچہ پیدا ہونے کے بعد رحم کا منہ کھل گیا اور انسان بھی پیدا ہو گیا جس سے لفظ نفاس مشتق ہے۔ اس لئے پہلے بچے کے بعد جو خون نکلے گا وہ سب نفاس شمار کیا جائے گا۔ اور امام محمد اور ز فر فر ماتے ہیں کہ ایک بچہ پیٹ میں موجود ہے اس لئے عورت ابھی حاملہ ہے اور حمل کی حالت میں جو خون آتا ہے وہ استحاضہ کا خون ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے پہلے بچے کے بعد جو خون ہے وہ استحاضہ کا خون ہوگا۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ ابھی رحم کا منہ بھی پورا کھلا ہوا نہیں ہے جب تک کہ دوسرا بچہ پیدا ہو کر منہ پورا نہ کھل جائے نفاس کا خون کیسے شمار کیا جائے گا۔ طرفین کی نظر بچہ پیدا ہونے کی طرف گئی اور امام محمد کی نظر اندر جو بچہ ابھی تک موجود ہے اس کی طرف گئی۔
بعد میں
And whoever gives birth to two children in one womb, her nifas is the blood that comes out after the first child according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them, and Muhammad and Zufar, may Allah have mercy on them, said: after the second child. The hadith was already mentioned in issue number 19. (Urdu: A woman delivered two children from one pregnancy. Her nifas is the blood that comes out after the first child according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar said: after the second child. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf say: after the first child is born, the mouth of the womb opens and a human is born, from which the word nifas is derived. Therefore, the blood that comes out after the first child will all be counted as nifas. Imam Muhammad and Zufar say that a child is still in the belly, so the woman is still pregnant, and blood that comes during pregnancy is istihadah. Therefore, the blood after the first child is istihadah. Another point is that the mouth of the womb is not fully opened until the second child is born; how can nifas blood be counted? The view of the two parties is directed towards the child born, while Imam Muhammad's view is directed towards the child still inside. Later...)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the definition of nifas (postpartum bleeding) in the case of twins. The core issue: when does nifas begin? According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, nifas starts with the first birth because the womb opens and a human is delivered, which is the etymological basis of the term nifas (derived from 'nufus' meaning 'soul' or 'birth'). Thus, any blood after the first child is nifas. In contrast, Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar argue that since a child remains in the womb, the woman is still pregnant, and bleeding during pregnancy is istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding). Therefore, nifas only begins after the second birth. The text also notes that a hadith supporting this ruling was already mentioned in issue 19. The dispute hinges on whether the presence of a remaining fetus negates the postpartum status. Later scholars may have preferred one view, but this passage does not specify which is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
النفاس (al-nifas): Postpartum bleeding following childbirth. In this dispute, it is defined as blood that emerges after the first child according to Abu Hanifa, or after the second child according to Muhammad.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Chronic non-menstrual bleeding that occurs outside the normal menstrual or postpartum period. Here, Muhammad argues that blood after the first twin is istihadah because pregnancy continues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, when does nifas begin for a woman giving birth to twins?
A) At the first birth
B) At the second birth
C) After 40 days
D) It is never considered nifas

Key Takeaway
For twin births, Hanafi imams disagree on when nifas begins: Abu Hanifa says after the first, Muhammad says after the second, affecting the woman's purity obligations in the interval.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Obligation of Purification from Najasah
Establishes obligatory purification from najasah for prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three components that must be purified from najasah for salah and identify the primary proof from the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Purification from physical impurity (najasah haqiqiyyah) is wajib on body, garment, and place; otherwise salah is invalid.

In this lesson, we begin the chapter on impurities (Babu al-Anjas) by establishing a foundational ruling: purification from najasah is wajib for three aspects related to salah. We will explore the Quranic and Hadith evidence that makes this a required condition for valid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The text states 'tatheer al-najasah waajib' – the obligation is wajib. The three items are: the worshiper's body, garment, and place of prayer.
Hanafis distinguish wajib from fard; this is wajib because the evidence is strong but not mutawatir.
2
Examine the primary Quranic proof
The verse 'wa thiyabaka fatahhir' (Surah al-Muddaththir 74:4) uses an imperative, which in Hanafi usul (al-amr yufidu al-wujub) indicates obligation. The command specifically mentions garments, but by qiyas it extends to body and place.
3
Analyze the hadith proofs
The hadith of Asma bint Abi Bakr instructs scratching and rinsing menstrual blood from clothing, proving garment purification. The hadith of Anas about bringing water for istinja proves body purification.
The hadith of the Prophet forbidding prayer in seven filthy places (e.g., garbage dump) indirectly proves place purification.
4
Understand the a fortiori reasoning
If purification from hukmiyyah (ritual impurity) is necessary, then from haqiqiyyah (physical impurity) – which is more unclean – is even more necessary. This is qiyas al-awla.
5
Conclude the practical requirement
For salah to be valid, the body, garment, and place must be free from najasah haqiqiyyah. If any is impure, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated after purification.
Small quantities that are excused (ma'fu 'anhu) are discussed in later chapters.

كتاب الطهارة
باب الانجاس
[۱۱۹](۱) تطهير النجاسة واجب من بدن المصلى وثوبه والمكان الذي يصلى عليه
باب الانجاس که
ضروری نوٹ انجاس نجس کی جمع ہے ناپا کی نجس کی دو قسمیں ہیں نجاست حکمیہ جیسے وضو اور غسل کی ضرورت ہو اور نجاست حقیقیہ جیسے پیشاب اور پاخانہ ۔ یہاں اسی نجاست حقیقیہ کے احکام کے متعلق بحث ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے وٹیا بک فطهر (آیت ۴ سورۃ المدثر ۷۴ ) اور حدیث یہ ہے عن اسماء بنت ابى بكر انها قالت سألت امرأة رسول الله علل الله فقالت يا رسول الله ارأيت احدانا اذا اصاب ثوبها الدم من الحيضة كيف تصنع فقال رسول الله اذا اصاب ثوب احداكن الدم من الحيضة فلتقرصه ثم لتنضحه بماء ثم لتصل فيه (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب غسل دم الحیض ص ۲۵ نمبر ۳۰۷ تر مندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی تغسل دم الحيض من الثوب ، ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۱۳۸) [119] (۱) نجاست کو پاک کرنا واجب ہے (۱) نماز پڑھنے والے کے بدن سے (۲) اس کے کپڑے سے (۳) اور اس مکان سے جس پر نماز پڑھتے ہیں۔
نماز پڑھنے والے کے لئے بدن، کپڑا اور مکان کا پاک ہونا ضروری ہے ورنہ نماز نہیں ہوگی۔ تجاست حکمیہ سے پاک ہونے کی دلیل تو وضو اور غسل کے ابواب میں گزری اور نجاست حقیقیہ سے پاک ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے۔ (۱) نجاست حکمیہ سے پاک ہونا ضروری ہے تو نجاست حقیقیہ مثلا پیشاب، پاخانہ لگا ہو تو اس سے پاک ہونا بدرجہ اولی ضروری ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو اور بھی زیادہ گندی چیز ہے (۲) بدن پاک ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے سمعت انس بن مالك يقول كان النبي اذا خرج لحاجته اجيء انا وغلام معنا ادارة من ماء یعنی يستنجی به (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الاستنجاء بالماء ص ۲۷ نمبر ۱۵۰) پانی سے استنجا کرنے کی وجہ یہی ہے کہ مصلی کا بدن نجاست حقیقیہ سے پاک ہونا چاہئے ۔ کپڑا پاک ہونے کی دلیل اوپر کی آیت۔ صلى الله وثیابک فطهر اور حدیث میں ہے عن اسماء ابنة ابى بكر ان امرأة سألت النبي الله عن الثوب يصيبه الدم من الـحـيـضـة؟ فقال رسول الله حتيه ثم اقرصيه بالماء ثم رشيه وصلى فيه (ج) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فى غسل دم الحيض من الثوب ص ۳۵ نمبر (۱۳۸) اور مکان پاک ہونے کی شرط کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عمران النبی نهى ان يصلى في سبعة مواطن في المزبلة والمجزرة والمقبرة وقارعة الطريق وفى الحمام و في معاطن الابل و فوق ظهر بيت الله (و) (ترندی حاشیہ : (الف) حضور کی بیوی نے آپ سے پوچھا کہ ہم میں سے ایک کے کپڑے کو حیض کا خون لگ جائے تو کیا کرے؟ آپ نے فرمایا تم میں سے کسی کے کپڑے کو حیض کا خون لگ جائے تو اس کو ہاتھ سے کھر چو پھر پانی سے دھوڈ پھر اس میں نماز پڑھو (ب) حضور جب اپنی ضرورت کے لئے نکلتے تو میں اور میرے ساتھ ایک لڑکا ہوتا۔ ہمارے ساتھ پانی کا برتن ہوتا یعنی آپ اس سے استنجا فرماتے ( ج ) حضور کی بیوی نے اس کپڑے کے بارے میں جس میں حیض کا خون لگ جائے پوچھا تو آپ نے فرمایا کھر جو پھر اس کو رگڑو پانی سے پھر اس پر پانی بہاؤ اور اس میں نماز پڑھو ( د ) آپ نے سات جگہ نماز پڑھنے سے منع فرمایا (۱) کھرا ( باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
Purification from impurity is obligatory from the body of the prayer, his garment, and the place he prays upon. (Urdu: Chapter of Impurities. Important note: 'Anjas' is the plural of 'najis'. There are two types of najasah: hukmiyyah, which requires wudu or ghusl, and haqiqiyyah, like urine and feces. Here the discussion is on the rulings of haqiqiyyah. Its proof is the verse 'And purify your garments' (74:4) and the hadith from Asma bint Abi Bakr: a woman asked the Prophet about blood from menstruation on her garment; he said: scratch it, then rinse with water, then pray in it. (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi) [119] (1) Purification from impurity is obligatory: (1) from the body of the prayer, (2) from his garment, (3) from the place he prays. For the prayer, the body, garment, and place must be pure; otherwise the prayer is invalid. The proof for purification from hukmiyyah came in the chapters of wudu and ghusl. The proof for haqiqiyyah is: (1) If purification from hukmiyyah is necessary, then from haqiqiyyah (like urine, feces) is even more necessary because it is more unclean. (2) The proof for body purification is the hadith that Anas ibn Malik said: When the Prophet went to relieve himself, I and a boy would bring a container of water for istinja. (Bukhari) The reason for istinja is that the body of the prayer must be pure from haqiqiyyah. The proof for garment purification is the above verse and the hadith from Asma about menstrual blood. The proof for the place is the hadith that the Prophet forbade praying in seven places: garbage dump, slaughterhouse, graveyard, middle of the road, bathroom, camel resting places, and on top of the Kaaba. (Tirmidhi, noted in margin).
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on impurities (Babu al-Anjas) and establishes the fundamental ruling that purification from najasah is wajib (obligatory) for three aspects of the prayer: the body of the worshiper, his garment, and the place where he prays. The author classifies najasah into two types: hukmiyyah (ritual impurity removed by wudu/ghusl) and haqiqiyyah (physical impurity like urine or blood). The focus here is haqiqiyyah. The proofs are drawn from the Quran (Surah al-Muddaththir 74:4: 'And purify your garments'), and from sunnah: the hadith of Asma bint Abi Bakr regarding menstrual blood on clothing instructing to scratch and rinse it, and the hadith of Anas about bringing water for istinja, indicating the necessity of body purification. Additionally, the reasoning of a fortiori (qiyas al-awla) is used: if purification from hukmiyyah is required, then from haqiqiyyah, which is more impure, is even more required. The hadith prohibiting prayer in seven filthy places (like garbage dumps and slaughterhouses) indirectly proves that the place must be pure. Thus, this lesson establishes a core fiqh principle for valid prayer.

Key Terms
النجاسة (al-najasah): Impurity. Divided into hukmiyyah (legal impurity requiring wudu/ghusl) and haqiqiyyah (physical impurity like urine, blood, feces). This chapter deals with the latter.
تطهير النجاسة (tatheer al-najasah): The act of purifying from impurity. Here, it is wajib on the body, garment, and place of prayer.
نجاسة حقيقية (najasah haqiqiyyah): Physical impurity that can be sensed (e.g., urine, feces, blood). It requires physical washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three things that must be purified from najasah for salah according to this passage?
A) The body of the worshiper
B) The garment
C) The place of prayer
D) The water used for wudu

Key Takeaway
Purification from physical impurity (najasah haqiqiyyah) is a wajib condition for the validity of salah, covering the body, garment, and place of prayer.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Obligation to Purify Najasah from Body, Clothing, and Place
Ruling on wajib purification of najasah from three sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying najasah before prayer and cite the Quranic and hadith evidence that support it.

Core Idea
Purification from najasah is wajib—a binding condition for prayer's validity.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling that purification from physical impurities is obligatory before prayer. The Hanafi school bases this on a clear Quranic command and prophetic instructions, establishing that the body, clothing, and place must be free from najasah for the prayer to be valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is purifying najasah from three sources: the body, clothing, and place of prayer. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory).
Wajib in Hanafi terminology means obligatory with zanni evidence, not fard from qat'i evidence.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites four proofs: Quran 74:4 (And purify your garments), the hadith of Asma regarding menstrual blood on clothing, the hadith of Anas about istinja with water, and the hadith of Ibn Umar forbidding prayer in places of impurity.
These proofs establish the obligation from both Quran and sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic imperative 'fatahhir' indicates wujub (al-amr yufidu al-wujub). The hadith of Asma commands a specific purification method, showing it is required. The hadith of Anas demonstrates the necessity of purifying the body. The hadith of Ibn Umar implies the place must be pure.
Each proof directly links to one of the three sources (body, clothing, place).
4
Note the madhhab position
The Hanafi school holds this ruling as wajib. There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the three imams agree. It is a condition (shart) for prayer, not a pillar.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih; some other schools classify it differently (e.g., fard), but all agree on its necessity.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, one must ensure body, clothing, and place are free from najasah before starting prayer. If any impurity is present, it must be removed; otherwise the prayer is invalid.
Small amounts may be excused per Hanafi details, but the basic obligation remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تطهير النجاسة واجب من بدن المصلى وثوبه والمكان الذي يصلى عليه
وَدَلِيلُهُ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {وَثِيَابَكَ فَطَهِّرْ} [المدثر: 4]
وَالْحَدِيثُ: عَنْ أَسْمَاءَ بِنْتِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: سَأَلَتِ امْرَأَةٌ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَرَأَيْتَ إِحْدَانَا إِذَا أَصَابَ ثَوْبَهَا الدَّمُ مِنَ الْحَيْضَةِ كَيْفَ تَصْنَعُ؟ فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: إِذَا أَصَابَ ثَوْبَ إِحْدَاكُنَّ الدَّمُ مِنَ الْحَيْضَةِ فَلْتَقْرِصْهُ ثُمَّ لَتَنْضَحْهُ بِمَاءٍ ثُمَّ لِتُصَلِّ فِيهِ. (متفق عليه)
وَعَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ قَالَ: كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِذَا خَرَجَ لِحَاجَتِهِ أَجِيءُ أَنَا وَغُلَامٌ مَعَنَا إِدَاوَةٌ مِنْ مَاءٍ يَسْتَنْجِي بِهِ. (رواه البخاري)
وَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَهَى أَنْ يُصَلَّى فِي سَبْعَةِ مَوَاطِنَ: فِي الْمَزْبَلَةِ، وَالْمَجْزَرَةِ، وَالْمَقْبَرَةِ، وَقَارِعَةِ الطَّرِيقِ، وَفِي الْحَمَّامِ، وَفِي مَعَاطِنِ الْإِبِلِ، وَفَوْقَ ظَهْرِ بَيْتِ اللَّهِ. (رواه الترمذي)
Purification of najasah is obligatory from the body of the one praying, his garment, and the place where he prays. Its evidence is His statement: 'And purify your garments' (74:4). And the hadith: From Asma bint Abi Bakr that a woman asked the Messenger of Allah... etc. And from Anas ibn Malik: 'When the Prophet would go to relieve himself, I would come with a boy carrying a vessel of water for him to perform istinja.' And from Ibn Umar that the Prophet forbade praying in seven places: the garbage dump, the slaughterhouse, the graveyard, the middle of the road, the bathroom, the places where camels are tied, and on top of the Kaaba.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that it is obligatory (wajib) to purify najasah from three things before prayer: the body, the clothing, and the place of prayer. The author provides four proofs: (1) the Quranic command 'And purify your garments' (74:4), which is a general command to purify oneself from all impurities; (2) the hadith of Asma regarding menstrual blood on clothing, where the Prophet instructed to rub it, rinse with water, and then pray in it, showing that purification is necessary; (3) the hadith of Anas about bringing water for istinja, proving the necessity of purifying the body; and (4) the hadith of Ibn Umar prohibiting prayer in places where impurity is likely, implying that the place must be pure. The Hanafi school holds that purification from najasah is a condition for the validity of prayer, and it is wajib to perform it before entering salat.

Key Terms
نجاسة (najāsah): Physical impurity, such as urine, feces, blood, etc., that must be removed for prayer.
تطهير (tat'hīr): The act of making something pure by removing najasah.
واجب (wājib): An obligation that must be fulfilled; omission incurs sin but does not invalidate the entire act if compensated? For purification, it is a condition, so absence invalidates prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Mandatory (fard)
B) Obligatory (wajib)
C) Recommended (sunnah)
D) Permissible (mubah)

Key Takeaway
Purification from najasah is a wajib condition for the validity of prayer, supported by Quran and hadith.

Permissibility of Purifying Najasah with Any Pure Liquid
Ruling on using non-water pure liquids for purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using non-water liquids for purification and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Any pure liquid that removes impurity suffices — water is not the only option.

In this passage, we learn that the Hanafi school permits using liquids like vinegar or rose water to remove ritual impurity from garments. This is based on the practice of Aisha using saliva. However, Imam Muhammad disagreed, arguing only water suffices. Let's explore the evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The author states that purification is permissible with water and any pure liquid that can remove the impurity. This expands the common understanding that only water works.
2
Examine the evidence
The hadith of Aisha shows her using saliva (a non-water liquid) to remove blood from her garment. The Prophet approved, indicating that the liquid need not be water.
Hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi objection
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that only water can purify najasah. He relies on the hadith of Asma which explicitly mentions water ('fltanta-huhu bi ma').
Imam Muhammad agrees with the Shafi'i school on this point.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the hadiths mentioning water do so because water is the most common medium, but they do not forbid other liquids. The objective is removal of impurity.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author prefers and the relied‐upon fatwa is Abu Hanifa's position: any pure liquid that removes impurity is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز تطهير النجاسة بالماء وبكل مائع طاهر يمكن ازالتها به كالخل و ماء الورد
وَدَلِيلُهُ: قَالَتْ عَائِشَةُ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهَا: مَا كَانَ لِأَحَدِنَا إِلَّا ثَوْبٌ وَاحِدٌ تَحِيضُ فِيهِ، فَإِذَا أَصَابَهُ شَيْءٌ مِنْ دَمٍ قَالَتْ: بِرِيقِهَا فَتَقْصَعُهُ بِظُفْرِهَا. (رواه البخاري وأبو داود)
It is permissible to purify najasah with water and every pure liquid that can remove it, such as vinegar and rose water. Its evidence: Aisha said: 'Each of us had only one garment in which she would menstruate. When any blood got on it, she would moisten it with her saliva and scrape it with her nail.'
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that purification of najasah is not restricted to water alone. Any liquid that is pure (tahir) and can remove the impurity, like vinegar or rose water, suffices. The proof is the hadith of Aisha where she used saliva to scrub bloodstains from her garment. Saliva is a liquid that is not water, yet the Prophet approved of this practice. This indicates that the aim is removing the impurity, not using a specific substance. The author then notes a dispute: Imam Muhammad (a Hanafi imam) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that only water can purify. They cite the hadith of Asma which specifically mentions water. The Hanafi response is that those hadith mention water as the most common purifier but do not preclude other liquids. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa, that any pure liquid that can remove the impurity is valid.

Key Terms
مائع (mā'i'): A liquid that flows, such as water, vinegar, rose water.
الخل (al-khall): Vinegar, an example of a pure liquid that can remove najasah.
ماء الورد (mā' al-ward): Rose water, another example of a pure liquid for purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only water
B) Water and any pure liquid that can remove the impurity
C) Only water or rose water
D) Only water or vinegar

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, any pure liquid that can physically remove najasah is sufficient for purification, even if it is not water.

Purification of Khuff from Dry Najasah by Rubbing
Ruling on purifying khuff from dry najasah with soil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying a khuff from dry najasah with substance and apply the condition of dryness to determine valid purification.

Core Idea
Dry impurity on khuff: rubbing on ground suffices; no water needed.

This lesson examines a specific but common scenario: a leather sock (khuff) becomes soiled with a dry impurity that has physical substance. The Hanafi school provides a practical ruling that simplifies purification, emphasizing the removal of the substance itself rather than the method. This ruling reflects the school's broader principle that the existence of impurity matters more than the means of removal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is purifying a khuff (leather sock) from najasah (impurity). The ruling is jā'iz (permissible) after performing the described action.
The ruling is specific to dry impurity with substance.
2
Note the conditions for the ruling
The najasah must have physical substance (jirm) and must be dry (yabis). Without either condition, the ruling does not apply.
Wet impurity requires washing with water.
3
Understand the method of purification
The method is rubbing (dalk) the khuff on the ground (al-ard) until the substance is removed. This suffices for purification.
The ground here acts as a tool for friction; it need not be clean soil.
4
Recognize the basis and inter-school difference
The basis is that removal of the physical impurity (jirm) is sufficient; the method is secondary. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require washing with water even for dry impurity.
This ikhtilaf has practical implications for daily worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اصابت الخف نجاسة ولها جرم فجفت فدلكه بالارض جاز
And if najasah with substance hits the khuff and it dries, then one rubs it on the ground, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This ruling addresses a specific case: if a khuff (leather sock) is soiled by a dry impurity that has body (jirm), such as dried mud, and the impurity dries, then rubbing the khuff on the ground until the impurity is removed purifies it. The Hanafi school allows this because the aim is removal of the physical impurity. This is based on the general principle that removal of the substance (jirm) suffices; washing is not required if the impurity is dry and can be brushed off. The text does not provide a specific proof here, but it follows from the broader Hanafi principle that the existence of the impurity is what matters, not the method of removal.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): Leather socks worn for footwear.
جرم (jirm): The physical substance of the impurity.
فجفت (fajaffat): It becomes dry.
فدلكه بالارض (fadalkahu bil-ard): Rubbing it on the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Must wash with water
B) Rubbing on the ground is sufficient
C) The socks must be discarded
D) Only water or rose water can be used

Key Takeaway
For a dry najasah with substance on a khuff, rubbing on the ground is a valid method of purification in the Hanafi school.

Purification with Any Thin Pure Liquid: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Establishes permissibility of purification with non-water thin liquids

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on purification with non-water liquids, identify the opposing view, and evaluate the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Any thin pure liquid can remove najasah; removal of impurity, not the medium, is what purifies.

In this lesson, we explore a key difference between the Hanafi school and other schools regarding purification. While many assume water is the only agent for taharah, the Hanafi school holds that any thin pure liquid suffices as long as it can wash away impurity. We will examine the evidence and reasoning behind this position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: It is permissible to purify najasah with any thin pure liquid (e.g., vinegar, rose water) that can remove it.
The key is the ability to wash away the impurity.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (within Hanafi school) and Imam Shafi'i hold that only water can purify.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of hadith.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The hadith of Aisha (رضي الله عنها) where she used saliva to moisten and remove blood from a cloth proves that any thin liquid suffices.
The hadith is in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
4
Analyze the opposing dalil
The opposing school cites hadiths that specifically mention using water, e.g., the hadith of Asma bint Abi Bakr about washing menstrual blood with water.
These hadiths do not explicitly exclude other liquids.
5
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that water is mentioned as a common practice, not as a requirement. The underlying principle is the removal of the najasah itself.
Thus, any thin pure liquid that can wash away the impurity is sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز تطهير النجاسة بالماء وبكل مائع طاهر يمكن ازالتها به کالخل و ماء الورد [۱](۳) واذا اصابت الخف نجاسة ولها جرم فجفت فدلكه بالارض جاز شریف ، باب ما جاء في كراهيته ما یصلی الیه و فید ص ۸۱ نمبر ۳۴۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان مقامات پر نا پا کی ہوتی ہے اس لئے ان مقامات پر نماز پڑھنا نا جائز ہے۔
[۲۰] (۲) نجاست کا پاک کرنا جائز ہے پانی کے ذریعہ اور ہروہ بہنے والی پاک چیز کے ذریعہ جن سے نجاست کا زائل کر ناممکن ہوجیسے سرکہ اور گلاب کا پانی۔ (۱) حنفیہ کے نزدیک اصل قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جن چیزوں سے نجاست کے اجزاء دھل جاتے ہیں وہ پانی نہ ہوں تب بھی ان چیزوں سے نجاست حقیقیہ کو پاک کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اصل ناپاکی تو اجزاء نجاست ہیں جب وہ ہی نہیں رہیں تو کپڑا پاک ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے گلاب کا پانی یا سر کہ جو پانی کی طرح پتلا ہوتے ہیں اور اجزاء نجاست کو دھو ڈالتے ہیں ان سے نجاست کو دھویا تو پاک ہو جائے گا۔ البتہ یہ رس کی قسموں میں سے ہیں اس لئے ان سے وضو یا غسل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے قالت عائشة ما كان لاحد انا الا ثوب واحد تحيض فيه فاذا اصابه شيء من دم قالت بريقها فقصعته بظفرها (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب هل تصلی المرأة في ثوب حاضت فیه ص ۴۵ نمبر ۳۱۲ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب المرأة تغسل ثوبها الذي تلبسه فيی حیضها ص ۵۸ نمبر ۳۶۴) آخری حدیث ہے۔ خون سب کے نزدیک ناپاک ہے اور اس کو تھوک سے تر کر کے ناخن سے رگڑ دیا اور خون زائل ہو گیا تو وہ چیز پاک ہو جائے گی (۳) جوتے پر نجاست لگی ہو اور زمین پر رگڑ دیا جائے اور نجاست زائل ہو جائے تو جو تا پاک ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ اصل قاعدہ یہی ہے کہ نجاست کے زیلان سے کپڑا پاک ہو جائے گا۔ امام محمد اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ صرف پانی سے نجاست زائل کرے گا تو پاک ہوگا۔کسی دوسری بہنے والی چیز سے نجاست زائل کرے گا تو چیز پاک نہیں ہوگی ۔ ان کی دلیل وہ احادیث ہیں جن میں پانی سے منی ، خون ، پیشاب پاک کرنے کا ذکر ہے۔ عن اسماء بنت ابی بكر ... اذا اصاب ثوب احداكن الدم من الحيضة فلتقرصه ثم لتنضحه بماء ثم لتصلى فيه ( بخاری شریف، باب غسل دم الحیض میں ۴۵ نمبر ۳۰۷) اس حدیث میں پانی سے ناپاکی دور کرنے کا تذکرہ ہے۔ اس لئے صرف پانی سے ناپا کی پاک ہوگی۔ مائع : ہر بننے والی چیز ، النخل : سرکا، ماء الورد : گلاب کا پانی۔
نوٹ جس بہنے والی چیز میں نجاست زائل کرنے کی صلاحیت نہ ہو اس سے کپڑا پاک نہیں ہوگا۔
It is permissible to purify najasah with water and with every pure liquid that can remove it, like vinegar and rose water. [20] (2) Purifying najasah is permissible by means of water and by every flowing pure thing by which removal of najasah is possible, like vinegar and rose water. (1) According to the Hanafis, the basic principle is that things with which the parts of najasah are washed away, even if they are not water, it is permissible to purify actual najasah with them. Because the original impurity is the parts of najasah; when they no longer remain, the cloth becomes pure. Therefore, rose water or vinegar, which are thin like water and wash away the parts of najasah, if najasah is washed with them, it becomes pure. However, they are types of juice, so it is not permissible to perform wudu or ghusl with them. The detail has passed before. (2) In a hadith: Aisha said, 'We did not have except one cloth in which we menstruated. When some blood got on it, she said she would moisten it with her saliva and scrape it off with her nail.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that blood is impure by consensus, and when she moistened it with saliva and scraped it with her nail, the blood was removed, so the thing became pure. (3) If a shoe has najasah on it and it is rubbed on the ground and the najasah is removed, the shoe becomes pure. The meaning of this is that the basic principle is that the cloth becomes pure by removal of najasah. Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i say that only if najasah is removed with water will it become pure; if najasah is removed with any other flowing thing, the thing will not become pure. Their evidence is the hadiths that mention purifying semen, blood, urine with water. From Asma bint Abi Bakr: 'When blood of menstruation gets on the garment of any one of you, she should scrape it, then sprinkle it with water, then pray in it.' (Bukhari) This hadith mentions removing impurity with water. Therefore, only with water will impurity become pure. Ma'i': every flowing thing, al-khal: vinegar, ma' al-ward: rose water. Note: A flowing thing that does not have the ability to remove najasah will not purify the cloth.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the means of purification from najasah. The Hanafi position holds that purification is achieved by the removal of the actual najasah substance, regardless of the medium used, as long as the medium is a thin pure liquid. Vinegar and rose water are given as examples. The commentary explains the underlying principle: impurity is the najasah particles themselves; when they are washed away, the item becomes pure. A hadith of Aisha is cited where she used saliva (a thin liquid) to moisten and scrape off blood from a cloth, proving that any thin liquid suffices. The opposing view of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam Shafi'i is that only water can purify, citing hadiths that specifically mention washing with water, such as the hadith of Asma. The Hanafi response is that those hadiths do not explicitly exclude other liquids; water is just the common medium. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view, as removal of najasah is the key.

Key Terms
مائع (ma'i'): A thin flowing liquid, as opposed to thick substances.
تطهير (tathir): The act of removing najasah to render something pure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following can be used to purify clothing from najasah?
A) Only water
B) Any thin pure liquid that can remove the najasah
C) Only vinegar
D) Any liquid, including oil

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows purification with any thin pure liquid that can remove najasah, based on the principle that physical removal of impurity, not the specific medium, is what matters.

Removing Dry Crusted Najasah from Leather: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on purifying leather shoes by rubbing off dried crusted najasah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on purifying leather shoes from dry crusted najasah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Rubbing on earth purifies dried solid najasah from leather; washing is not required.

This lesson examines a practical issue of purification: when a leather shoe becomes soiled with solid najasah (like dung) that dries, can it be purified simply by rubbing on earth? The Hanafi school answers yes, relying on a specific hadith and the principle that removal of dry solid najasah suffices. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, insisting on washing. We will unpack the proofs and the legal reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: rubbing on earth removes dry solid najasah from leather, purifying the item for prayer.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Shafi'i holds that washing is required; rubbing does not purify.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i reliance on the general principle that najasah must be washed away.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine how Hanafis use the hadith of Abu Huraira and distinguish between wet and dry najasah; dry solid najasah is removed by friction.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: Hanafis consider prayer valid after rubbing; Shafi'is require washing for prayer to be valid.

Source Text

[۱۱۲۱ (۳) اگر موزے کو ایسی نجاست لگ جائے جس کو جسم ہے پھر وہ خشک ہو جائے پس اس کو رگڑ دے زمین سے تو اس موزے میں نماز الصلوة فيه [۱۲] (۴) والمنى نجس يجب غسل رطبه.
جائز ہے لی جس نجاست کو جسم ہے جیسے پاخانہ ، لید ، گوبر وغیرہ وہ چمڑے کے موزے یا جوتے پر لگ جائے پھر خشک ہو جائے پھر اس کو زمین سے اتنا رگڑ دے کہ پاخانہ لگا ہوا محسوس نہ ہو تو وہ جو تا یا موزہ پاک ہو جائے گا۔
(۱) چمڑے میں جو نا پا کی سرایت کی ہوگی وہ کم ہے اور سوکھنے کی وجہ سے ناپاکی کے جسم نے واپس چوس لیا اور چمڑے کے اندر بہت کم نا پا کی رہ گئی اور اوپر کے حصے کو زمین سے رگڑ دیا تو نجاست زائل ہو گئی اور پہلے بتایا گیا ہے کہ نجاست کے زائل ہونے سے کپڑا یا چمڑا پاک ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ جوتے یا موزے پاک ہو جائیں گے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال اذا وطى احدكم بنعله الأذى فان التراب له طهور (الف) ( ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی الاذی یصیب افعل ص ۶۱ نمبر ۳۸۵ باب الصلوۃ في الفعل، نمبر ۶۵۰ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مٹی سے رگڑنے کے بعد جو تا یا موزہ پاک ہو جائے گا۔
اصول نجاست حقیقیہ کے زائل ہونے سے چیز پاک ہو جائیگی۔
جرم : جسم دار، جفت : خشک ہو گیا، دلک : رگڑا۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ موزے میں نجاست لگ جائے تو بغیر دھوئے پاک نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ رگڑنے کی وجہ سے نجاست پھر بھی موزے پر رہ جائے گی اور احادیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نجاست کو دھوئے بغیر پاک نہیں ہوتی۔
نون ترنجاست دھونے سے پاک ہوگی۔
(3) If a leather sock (khuff) gets najasah that has volume (jirm), then it dries, and he rubs it on the ground, then it is permissible to pray in it. It is permissible for that najasah which has volume, like stool, dung, etc., to get on a leather sock or shoe, then it dries, then he rubs it on the ground until the stuck stool is not felt, then that shoe or sock becomes pure. (1) The penetration of najasah in the leather is little, and due to drying, the body of najasah has absorbed back, and very little najasah remained inside the leather, and the upper part was rubbed on the ground, so the najasah was removed. And it was stated earlier that by removal of najasah, cloth or leather becomes pure. Therefore, these shoes or socks become pure. (2) In a hadith: Abu Huraira reported that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When one of you steps on filth with his sandal, then earth is a purifier for it.' (Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that after rubbing with earth, the shoe or sock becomes pure. Principle: By removal of actual najasah, the thing becomes pure. Jirm: having volume, jaffa: became dry, dalk: rubbing. Imam Shafi'i says that if najasah gets on a sock, it does not become pure without washing, because due to rubbing, najasah still remains on the sock, and hadiths indicate that najasah is not purified without washing. Note: najasah is purified by washing.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on purifying leather items from dry crusted najasah. The Hanafi ruling states that if solid najasah (e.g., stool, dung) adheres to a leather sock or shoe and dries, then rubbing it on the ground until no trace remains renders the item pure. The commentary explains that the leather absorbs minimal najasah; drying causes the najasah to be reabsorbed into its solid mass, and rubbing removes the surface portion, leaving the item pure. The principle is that physical removal of najasah purifies. A hadith of Abu Huraira is cited where the Prophet said that earth purifies the sandal after stepping on filth. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that rubbing does not fully remove najasah; washing is required. The Hanafi response relies on the principle of removal and the hadith. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
جرم (jirm): The solid volume or body of the najasah, as opposed to thin liquid najasah.
دلك (dalk): Rubbing or scratching to remove a substance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, if a leather shoe gets dry stool on it, how can it be purified?
A) It must be washed with water
B) It becomes pure by rubbing on earth until no trace remains
C) It cannot be purified; the shoe must be discarded
D) It is automatically pure because of the leather

Key Takeaway
Dry crusted solid najasah on leather is removed by rubbing on earth, making the item pure; this is a Hanafi concession based on a specific hadith.

Impurity of Semen and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling that semen is impure and must be washed while wet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the impurity of semen and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Semen is najis in Hanafi fiqh; washing it while wet is wajib.

This passage establishes the Hanafi position that semen (maniy) is impure and must be washed while still wet, based on the practice of Aisha (ra) and a hadith listing five impurities. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, holding semen to be pure. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for applying the correct ruling in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the ruling: semen is najis, and its wet part must be washed (wajib).
This applies to clothing and body.
2
Identify the Opposing School
Note that Imam Shafi'i holds semen is pure and does not require washing.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the Hanafi Proof
Analyze the hadith of Aisha washing semen from the Prophet's garment and the hadith listing five impurities including semen.
The hadith demonstrate najasah.
4
Consider the Shafi'i Proof
Although not detailed in the text, Shafi'i relies on hadiths suggesting semen is like spittle, implying purity.
The Hanafi response is that Aisha's practice overrides.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
Hanafi: clothing with semen must be washed before prayer; Shafi'i: prayer is valid without washing.
This thamarah al-khilaf affects daily practice.

[۱۲] (۴) والمنى نجس يجب غسل رطبه.
(1) منی نکلنے سے غسل واجب ہوتا ہے۔ جس چیز پر غسل واجب ہو ظاہر ہے کہ وہ چیز خود بھی ناپاک ہوگی (۲) حدیث میں ہے حضرت عائشہ تر منی کو حضور کے کپڑے سے دھویا کرتی تھی اگر وہ ناپاک نہ ہوتی تو دھونے کی ضرورت نہیں تھی ۔ حدیث میں ہے سألت عائشة عن الـمـنـى يصيب الثوب؟ فقالت كنت اغسله من ثوب رسول الله الله فيخرج الى الصلوة و اثر الغسل في ثوبه بقع الماء (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب غسل المنی و فر که ص ۳۶ نمبر ۲۳۰ ر مسلم شریف ، باب حکم المنی ص ۱۴۰ نمبر ۲۸۹) دوسری حدیث ہے یا عمارانما يغسل الثوب من خمس، من الغائط والبول والقيء والدم والمنى (دار قطنی ، باب نجاسة البول والامر بالمنتزه منهج اول ص ۱۳۴ نمبر ۲ ۴۵ ) فائدہ امام مالک کا بھی یہی مسلک ہے۔

(4) Semen is impure; it is obligatory to wash its wet part. (1) From the emission of semen, ghusl becomes obligatory. The thing that necessitates ghusl is obviously itself impure. (2) Aisha used to wash wet semen from the garment of the Prophet; if it were not impure, washing would not be necessary. In a hadith: Aisha was asked about semen getting on the garment; she said, 'I used to wash it from the garment of the Messenger of Allah, and he would go out to prayer while the mark of washing was on his garment as a water spot.' (Bukhari, Muslim) Another hadith: 'O Ammar, the garment is washed from five things: from feces, urine, vomit, blood, and semen.' (Dar Qutni) Benefit: Imam Malik also holds this view. According to Imam Shafi'i, semen is pure. If it gets on clothing, washing is not necessary. His evidence is (1) the hadiths that...
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the impurity (najasah) of semen. The Hanafi position is that semen is najis, and it is wajib to wash it while wet. The reasoning is that semen necessitates ghusl, so it must be impure. The hadith of Aisha is cited where she washed semen from the Prophet's garment, proving its impurity. Another hadith lists semen among five impurities that require washing. Imam Malik agrees with this view. Imam Shafi'i holds that semen is pure and does not require washing. The commentator mentions that Shafi'i relies on different hadiths. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that semen is najis, and washing the wet part is obligatory.

Key Terms
مني (maniy): Semen, the fluid emitted at orgasm.
رطب (ratb): Wet, as opposed to dry. The ruling applies to wet semen specifically.

D) The garment must be discarded

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, semen is impure (najis) and must be washed while wet; the Shafi'i school holds it is pure.

Purification of Earth by the Sun
Ruling with proof on purification of earth by the sun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purification of earth by the sun and explain the evidence supporting it from hadith and practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Earth becomes pure for prayer when impurity dries and traces vanish, but tayammum requires absolutely pure earth.

This passage addresses a practical question: if impurity falls on earth and later dries completely, is the earth pure? The Hanafi school answers yes for prayer, but no for tayammum. The ruling is based on the practice of the Companions and the principle of ease, differentiating between wet and dry impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the purification of earth affected by najasa. The ruling: prayer on that spot is permissible (the earth is considered pure for prayer). Tayammum from that earth is not permissible because the earth is not absolutely pure.
Tayammum requires the earth to be 'tayyib' (pure) per Quran 5:6.
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides two proofs: (1) The practice of Abdullah ibn Umar who saw dogs urinate in the mosque and no one washed it, yet prayer continued. (2) The statement of Abu Qilaba, a tabi'i, that when earth dries it becomes purified.
These are ahad hadith and athar, but accepted in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The absence of washing in the presence of the Prophet (peace be upon him) indicates tacit approval. If drying did not purify, the Prophet would have ordered washing. Abu Qilaba's explicit statement confirms the principle.
This shows that the Prophet's silence (taqrir) is a form of Sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar hold that earth does not become pure even after drying; it must be washed. They cite the hadith where the Prophet ordered water to be poured on a Bedouin's urine in the mosque.
The Hanafis respond by distinguishing wet vs. dry impurity.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafis argue that the hadith of the Bedouin applies to wet impurity (the urine was fresh). For dry impurity, the practice of the Companions and the statement of Abu Qilaba are stronger evidence. The principle of ease (taysir) also supports the Hanafi view.
The mufta bihi is that earth becomes pure by drying when traces are gone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۲۵ (۷) وان اصابت الارض نجاسة فجفت باشمس وذهب اثرها جازت الصلوة على مكانها ولا يجوز التيمم منها.
[۱۲] (۷) اگر زمین پر ناپا کی لگ جائے اور سورج اس کو خشک کر دے اور ناپاکی کا اثر ختم ہو جائے تو اس جگہ پر نماز جائز ہے اور اس سے تیم جائز نہیں ہے۔
پیشاب یا پاخانہ یا کوئی اور نا پا کی زمین پر لگی ہولیکن سورج نے اس ناپاکی کو خشک کردیا اور ناپاکی کا اثرات ختم ہو گئے اب پتہ نہیں چلتا کہ اس جگہ پیشاب یا پاخانہ تھا تو اب وہ جگہ پاک ہو گئی اس پر نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ تمیم کرنا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ آیت قرآنی سے اس کے لئے مٹی کا بالکل پاک ہونا ضروری ہے فتيمموا صعيدا طيبا بالکل پاک مٹی کی قید ہے۔
(۱) حدیث میں ہے قال عبد الله ابن عمر كنت ابيت في المسجد في عهد رسول الله له و كنت فتى شابا عزبا، وكانت الكلاب تبول و تقبل وتدبر في المسجد فلم يكونوا يرشون شيئا من ذلک (الف) (ابوداہد شریف، باب في طهور الارض اذا يبست ص ۶۰ نمبر ۳۸۲) (۲) عن ابي قلابة قال اذا جفت الارض فقد زكت (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۷۲ من قال اذا کانت جافة فھو ز کا تہا ، ج اول ص ۵۹ نمبر ۶۲۵)
کتا مسجد میں پیشاب کرتا ہو پھر اس کو کوئی دھوتا نہ ہو اور اسی پر نماز پڑھتا ہو یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ پیشاب خشک ہونے کے بعد اور اس کے اثرات چلے جانے کے بعد جگہ پاک ہوگئی۔ ابو قلابہ کے قول میں تو صاف ہے کہ زمین خشک ہوگئی تو پاک ہوگئی۔
نوں نجاست تر ہو یا اس کے اثرات نہ گئے ہوں تو دھوئے بغیر زمین پاک نہیں ہوگی۔
نا که امام شافعی اور امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ نجاست خشک ہونے اور اثرات جانے کے بعد بھی دھوئے بغیر زمین پاک نہیں ہوگی۔ (۱) پاک کرنے والی کوئی چیز نہیں پائی گئی (۲) حدیث میں ہے ان ابا هريرة قال قام اعرابي قبال في المسجد فتناوله الناس فقال لهم النبي عل الله دعوه وهر يقوا على بوله سجلا من ماء او ذنوبا من ماء فانما بعثتم ميسرين لم تبعثوا معسرين (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب صب الماء على البول في المسجد ص ۳۵ نمبر ۲۲۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زمین پر پانی بہانے سے پاک ہوگی۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ تر نجاست ہو تو ہم بھی کہتے ہیں کہ پانی بہانے سے پاک ہوگی۔ یہاں پیشاب تر تھا اور جلدی میں نماز پڑھنی تھی اس لئے پانی سے پاک کی گئی۔ البتہ خشک کے لئے اوپر کی حدیث پر عمل ہوا۔ فت جفت : خشک ہوگئی۔
حاشیه : (الف) عبداللہ ابن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ میں حضور کے زمانے میں مسجد میں رات گڑاتا تھا۔ میں جوان اکیلا تھا۔ کتا پیشاب کرتا تھا اور مسجد میں آتا جاتا تھا تو کوئی بھی اس پر پانی نہیں چھر کتا تھا (ب) ابو قلابہ نے فرمایا جب زمین خشک ہو جائے تو پاک ہو جائے گی (ج) ابو ہریرۃ نے فرمایا ایک دیہاتی کھڑے ہوئے اور مسجد میں پیشاب کرنے لگے۔ لوگوں نے ان کو جھڑکنا شروع کیا تو حضور نے ان لوگوں سے کہا اس کو چھوڑ دو اور اس کے پیشاب پر ایک ڈول پانی بہا دو سجلا کہا یا ذنوبا کیا ) تم لوگ آسانی کے ساتھ بھیجے گئے ہوں تنگی کے ساتھ نہیں بھیجے گئے ہوں۔]
If impurity affects the earth and it dries by the sun and its trace goes away, prayer on that place is permissible, but tayammum from it is not permissible. (Urdu explanation follows: If urine or stool or any other impurity gets on the earth, and the sun dries it and the trace of impurity disappears, now it is not known that there was urine or stool in that place, so that place has become pure. Prayer on it is permissible. Tayammum is not permissible because the Quranic verse requires the earth to be absolutely pure: 'Fataimmu saeedan tayyiban' - pure earth is a condition.) (1) Hadith: Abdullah ibn Umar said: I used to spend the night in the mosque in the time of the Messenger of Allah, and I was a young unmarried man. Dogs used to urinate, come and go in the mosque, and they did not sprinkle anything of that. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Tahur al-Ard idha yabisat, p.60 no.382) (2) Abu Qilaba said: When the earth dries, it becomes purified. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 72, from 'man qala idha kanat jaffatan fahuwa zakat' vol.1 p.59 no.625) - The dog urinating in the mosque and no one washing it, and praying on it, is evidence that after the urine dries and its traces go, the place becomes pure. Abu Qilaba's statement is clear: when the earth dries, it becomes pure. However, if the impurity is wet or its traces have not gone, the earth will not become pure without washing. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Zufar say that even after the impurity dries and traces go, the earth will not become pure without washing. (1) No purifying agent is found. (2) Hadith: Abu Huraira said: A Bedouin stood and urinated in the mosque. The people started to rebuke him. The Prophet said: Leave him, and pour a bucket of water over his urine. Verily you have been sent to make things easy, not to make things difficult. (Bukhari, Bab Sabb al-Maa' ala al-Bawli fi al-Masjid, p.35 no.220) This hadith shows that the earth becomes pure by pouring water. We say: If the impurity is wet, we also say that it becomes pure by pouring water. Here the urine was wet and prayer was needed quickly, so it was purified with water. But for dry impurity, the above hadith is acted upon. 'Fajaffat': became dry. Footnotes: (a) Abdullah ibn Umar says: I used to spend the night in the mosque in the Prophet's time. I was young and single. Dogs urinated, came and went in the mosque, and no one sprinkled water on it. (b) Abu Qilaba said: When the earth becomes dry, it becomes pure. (c) Abu Huraira said: A Bedouin stood and urinated in the mosque. People started to stop him. The Prophet said to them: Leave him, and pour a bucket of water over his urine. 'Sajlan' or 'Dhanuban' - a bucket. You have been sent with ease, not with hardship.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the purification of earth by the sun. The base ruling states that if the earth is affected by impurity and the sun dries it and removes all traces, prayer on that spot is permissible, but tayammum with that earth is not allowed. The commentary explains that the impurity could be urine, stool, or any other najasa. Once dried and traces gone, the place is considered pure for prayer. However, for tayammum, the earth must be absolutely pure (tahir) as per the Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah: 6), which requires 'sa'eedan tayyiban'. The proof comes from the practice of the Companions: Ibn Umar reports that dogs urinated in the mosque during the Prophet's time and no one washed it, yet prayer continued there. Also the statement of Abu Qilaba, a tabi'i, that when earth dries it becomes purified. The text then addresses the objection of Imams Shafi'i and Zufar, who hold that even if dry, the earth remains impure unless washed. The Hanafi response distinguishes between wet and dry impurity: the hadith of the Bedouin (where the Prophet ordered water to be poured on urine) applies to wet impurity, while the case of dry impurity follows the practice of the Companions and the principle of ease. Thus, the Hanafi position is that once the impurity is dry and traces gone, the earth becomes pure without washing. This is a matter of istihsan based on custom and ease.

Key Terms
نجاسة (najāsa): Impurity, especially liquid or solid that prevents validity of prayer.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with earth; requires earth to be absolutely pure (tayyib).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if urine dries on the ground by the sun and its trace disappears, what is the ruling for prayer on that spot?
A) Prayer is not valid until washed.
B) Prayer is valid but tayammum is not allowed.
C) Both prayer and tayammum are valid.
D) Prayer is invalid even if dry.

Key Takeaway
Earth becomes pure for prayer by the sun when impurity dries and no trace remains, but it is not pure enough for tayammum.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Amount of Heavy Impurity Excused in Prayer
Ruling on the quantity of heavy impurity excused on body/clothes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the quantity of heavy impurity excused in prayer and identify the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Less than a dirham of heavy impurity is excused; a dirham or more invalidates prayer.

Purity is essential for prayer, but Islamic law is not burdensome. The Hanafi school teaches that a small amount of heavy impurity—the size of a dirham or less—does not invalidate prayer. This concession is rooted in prophetic practice, as shown by the hadiths on istinja with stones and the explicit mention of a dirham of blood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: the presence of heavy impurity on the body or clothes during prayer. The ruling: if the impurity is a dirham or less, prayer is valid; if more, it is invalid.
Heavy impurity includes blood, urine, feces, and wine.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two ahadith: (1) The hadith of istinja with stones from Aisha, which shows that a small residue of impurity after cleaning with stones is excused. (2) The hadith of Abu Huraira that 'prayer is repeated for the amount of a dirham of blood,' implying less is excused.
Both hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The istinja hadith indicates that a trace amount (equivalent to the size of the anus, about a dirham) is permissible without full washing. The blood hadith directly sets a dirham as the threshold for invalidation, so less than that is forgiven.
The dirham is defined as the width of the palm.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Shafi'i and Imam Zufar hold that any amount, no matter how small, must be washed because the general commands to wash impurity apply without exception.
Their proof is general hadiths like 'Wash your garment from impurity.'
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school gives precedence to the specific concessions (rukhsa) from the ahadith, arguing that the Shariah does not intend hardship. The evidence from istinja and the explicit dirham threshold overrides the general commands by way of takhsis.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.

If heavy impurity like blood, urine, feces, and wine touches a person, the amount of a dirham or less, then prayer with it is permissible. If it exceeds that, it is not permissible. (Urdu: If heavy impurity gets on body or clothes and it is less than a dirham i.e. the width of the palm, then prayer without washing is valid, though washing is necessary. (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Istinja' bi al-Ahjar, p. no.40) The area of excretion is the size of a dirham or the depth of the palm, so that amount is excused. If more than that is present, prayer without washing is not valid. Hadith from Abu Huraira: The Prophet said: Prayer is repeated for the amount of a dirham of blood. Therefore even a little impurity must be washed for prayer to be valid. Heavy impurity: that impurity on whose impurity there is consensus is heavy impurity. And that about which scholars disagree is not heavy. The evidence that blood, human urine, and feces are heavy impurity is the hadith: O Ammar, the garment is washed from five things: feces, urine, vomit, blood, and semen. (Dar Qutni, Bab Najasat al-Bawl wal-Amr bi al-Nazaha minhu, vol.1 p.134 no.452) The evidence for wine being impure is the hadith from Abu Thalaba al-Khushani that he asked the Prophet: We deal with the People of the Book, and they cook pork in their pots and drink wine in their vessels.
